Question 1 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Please fill the blank field(s) in the statement with the right words. The built-in Jinja macro that returns `True` only during incremental runs when the destination table already exists and `--full-refresh` is not set is called __()

  [+] A. is_incremental
       -> The `is_incremental()` macro returns `True` when three conditions are met: the model is materialized as `incremental`, the destination table already exists, and `--full-refresh` is not set. It is typically used inside `{% if %}` blocks to gate a WHERE clause that filters for new rows only.

Question 2 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A model at `models/dim/dim_listings_cleansed.sql` contains this config block: {{ config(materialized = 'view') }} The project's `dbt_project.yml` sets: models : airbnb : + materialized : view dim : + materialized : table src : + materialized : ephemeral How will `dim_listings_cleansed` be materialized?

  [ ] A. As a table, because the `dim/` folder setting in `dbt_project.yml` takes precedence
       -> Incorrect. The `dim/` folder setting in `dbt_project.yml` is less specific than the in-file `config()` block.
  [+] B. As a view, because the in-file `config()` block takes precedence over `dbt_project.yml`
       -> Correct. The in-file `config()` block is the most specific config level and always takes precedence over `dbt_project.yml` settings.
  [ ] C. As ephemeral, because the project-level default applies to all models
       -> Incorrect. The `src/` folder's ephemeral setting does not apply to models in the `dim/` folder.
  [ ] D. It will raise a compilation error due to conflicting configurations
       -> Incorrect. Conflicting configs do not cause errors -- dbt simply uses the most specific one.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The `dim/` folder setting in `dbt_project.yml` is less specific than the in-file `config()` block. - **B) Correct.** The in-file `config()` block is the most specific config level and always takes precedence over `dbt_project.yml` settings. - **C) Incorrect.** The `src/` folder's ephemeral setting does not apply to models in the `dim/` folder. - **D) Incorrect.** Conflicting configs do not cause errors -- dbt simply uses the most specific one. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/model-configs#configuring-models

Question 3 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A developer runs the following command: dbt run -- select + dim_listings_w_hosts Looking at the lineage graph above, which models does this command build?

  [ ] A. Only `dim_listings_w_hosts` itself, without selecting any upstream or downstream models in the DAG
       -> Incorrect. Without the `+` prefix, only `dim_listings_w_hosts` itself would be selected. The `+` prefix adds all upstream ancestors.
  [ ] B. `dim_listings_w_hosts` and all of its downstream dependents
       -> Incorrect. The `+` prefix selects upstream ancestors, not downstream dependents. For downstream selection, you would place `+` as a suffix: `dim_listings_w_hosts+`.
  [+] C. `dim_listings_w_hosts` and all upstream ancestors: `dim_listings_cleansed`, `src_listing, `dim_hosts_cleansed`, and `src_hosts`
       -> Correct. The `+` prefix in `+dim_listings_w_hosts` selects the model and all its upstream ancestors. From the lineage graph, this includes both branches: `src_listings` -> `dim_listings_cleansed` and `src_hosts` -> `dim_hosts_cleansed`.
  [ ] D. Every model in the entire project, as they are all affected by `dim_listings_w_hosts`
       -> Incorrect. The `+` prefix only traverses the upstream lineage of the specified model. Unrelated branches like `fct_reviews` and `mart_fullmoon_reviews` are not selected.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Without the `+` prefix, only `dim_listings_w_hosts` itself would be selected. The `+` prefix adds all upstream ancestors. - **B) Incorrect.** The `+` prefix selects upstream ancestors, not downstream dependents. For downstream selection, you would place `+` as a suffix: `dim_listings_w_hosts+`. - **C) Correct.** The `+` prefix in `+dim_listings_w_hosts` selects the model and all its upstream ancestors. From the lineage graph, this includes both branches: `src_listings` -> `dim_listings_cleansed` and `src_hosts` -> `dim_hosts_cleansed`. - **D) Incorrect.** The `+` prefix only traverses the upstream lineage of the specified model. Unrelated branches like `fct_reviews` and `mart_fullmoon_reviews` are not selected. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/graph-operators

Question 4 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO of the following statements about ephemeral models are true? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. They do not create any tables or views in the database -- their SQL is injected as CTEs into downstream models
       -> Correct. Ephemeral models create no database objects; dbt interpolates their SQL as CTEs into downstream models.
  [ ] B. They persist as temporary tables in the warehouse between runs
       -> Incorrect. Ephemeral models do not persist at all -- they create no tables (temporary or otherwise) in the warehouse.
  [+] C. They cannot be queried directly in the data warehouse
       -> Correct. Because nothing is materialized in the database, ephemeral models cannot be queried directly in the warehouse.
  [ ] D. They cannot be referenced using `ref()` from other models
       -> Incorrect. Ephemeral models can be referenced using `ref()` from other models -- that is how their SQL gets injected as CTEs.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Ephemeral models create no database objects; dbt interpolates their SQL as CTEs into downstream models. - **B) Incorrect.** Ephemeral models do not persist at all -- they create no tables (temporary or otherwise) in the warehouse. - **C) Correct.** Because nothing is materialized in the database, ephemeral models cannot be queried directly in the warehouse. - **D) Incorrect.** Ephemeral models can be referenced using `ref()` from other models -- that is how their SQL gets injected as CTEs. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/materializations#ephemeral

Question 5 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Consider this line from an incremental model: {{ dbt_utils . generate_surrogate_key ([ 'listing_id' , 'review_date' , 'reviewer_name' , 'review_text' ]) }} as review_id What does `dbt_utils.generate_surrogate_key()` produce?

  [ ] A. An auto-incrementing integer starting from 1 for each row in the result set
       -> Incorrect. `generate_surrogate_key()` does not produce auto-incrementing integers -- it produces hash values.
  [+] B. A deterministic hash value based on the combination of the specified columns
       -> Correct. `generate_surrogate_key()` creates a deterministic hash (typically MD5) from the concatenation of the provided column values. For the same inputs it always produces the same hash, making it ideal for stable surrogate keys.
  [ ] C. A random UUID generated fresh on every run, unique across all executions
       -> Incorrect. The hash is deterministic, not random -- the same inputs always produce the same output.
  [ ] D. A composite primary key constraint applied to the listed columns in the warehouse
       -> Incorrect. It does not create a database constraint; it generates a computed column value.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `generate_surrogate_key()` does not produce auto-incrementing integers -- it produces hash values. - **B) Correct.** `generate_surrogate_key()` creates a deterministic hash (typically MD5) from the concatenation of the provided column values. For the same inputs it always produces the same hash, making it ideal for stable surrogate keys. - **C) Incorrect.** The hash is deterministic, not random -- the same inputs always produce the same output. - **D) Incorrect.** It does not create a database constraint; it generates a computed column value. Reference: https://github.com/dbt-labs/dbt-utils#generate_surrogate_key

Question 6 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Examine this model: SELECT listing_id , listing_name , room_type , CASE WHEN minimum_nights = 0 THEN 1 ELSE minimum_nights END AS minimum_nights , host_id , REPLACE ( price_str , '$' ) :: NUMBER ( 10 , 2 ) AS price , created_at , updated_at FROM src_listings Which TWO business rules does this model enforce? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. Listings with `minimum_nights = 0` are replaced with `1` to ensure a minimum one-night stay
       -> Correct. The CASE expression replaces `minimum_nights = 0` with `1`, enforcing a minimum one-night stay.
  [+] B. The `price_str` column is cleansed by removing the `$` sign and casting to a numeric type
       -> Correct. The `REPLACE(price_str, '$') :: NUMBER(10, 2)` expression strips the dollar sign and casts the result to a numeric type.
  [ ] C. Listings with no reviews are filtered out by a WHERE clause before transformation
       -> Incorrect. There is no WHERE clause or filter on reviews in this SQL -- no rows are filtered out before transformation.
  [ ] D. Host names are defaulted to `'Anonymous'` when NULL using a COALESCE expression
       -> Incorrect. There is no COALESCE or defaulting logic for host names in this SQL. The model does not reference host names at all.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** The CASE expression replaces `minimum_nights = 0` with `1`, enforcing a minimum one-night stay. - **B) Correct.** The `REPLACE(price_str, '$') :: NUMBER(10, 2)` expression strips the dollar sign and casts the result to a numeric type. - **C) Incorrect.** There is no WHERE clause or filter on reviews in this SQL -- no rows are filtered out before transformation. - **D) Incorrect.** There is no COALESCE or defaulting logic for host names in this SQL. The model does not reference host names at all. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/best-practices/how-we-structure/3-intermediate

Question 7 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
An incremental model uses `var("start_date")` and `var("end_date")` for date filtering: {% if is_incremental () %} {% if var ( "start_date" , False ) and var ( "end_date" , False ) %} AND review_date >= '{{ var("start_date") }}' AND review_date < '{{ var("end_date") }}' {% else %} AND review_date > ( select max ( review_date ) from {{ this }}) {% endif %} {% endif %} A developer runs: `dbt run --select fct_reviews --vars '{"start_date": "2024-01-01"}'` (without providing `end_date`). What happens?

  [ ] A. dbt raises a compilation error because `end_date` is not defined in the project `vars` config
       -> Incorrect. `var('end_date', False)` returns `False` (the default) rather than raising an error, because a default value is provided in the macro call.
  [+] B. The model falls back to standard incremental logic (`review_date > max(review_date)`) via short-circuit evaluation
       -> Correct. The Jinja `and` uses Python-style short-circuit evaluation. `var('end_date', False)` returns `False`, so the condition evaluates to `False` and execution falls to the `{% else %}` block using standard `max(review_date)` logic.
  [ ] C. The model loads all historical data from `start_date` onward with no upper bound on `end_date`
       -> Incorrect. The model does not load all data from `start_date` onward because the `and` condition fails, sending execution to the else block.
  [ ] D. dbt ignores both variables because they must always be provided together as a pair
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not require variables to be provided together. Each `var()` call is evaluated independently with its own default value.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `var('end_date', False)` returns `False` (the default) rather than raising an error, because a default value is provided in the macro call. - **B) Correct.** The Jinja `and` uses Python-style short-circuit evaluation. `var('end_date', False)` returns `False`, so the condition evaluates to `False` and execution falls to the `{% else %}` block using standard `max(review_date)` logic. - **C) Incorrect.** The model does not load all data from `start_date` onward because the `and` condition fails, sending execution to the else block. - **D) Incorrect.** dbt does not require variables to be provided together. Each `var()` call is evaluated independently with its own default value. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/dbt-jinja-functions/var

Question 8 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Which statement about `env_var()` and `var()` is correct?

  [ ] A. Both can be used in `dbt_project.yml` and in model SQL files with no restrictions on context
       -> Incorrect. `var()` cannot be used in `dbt_project.yml` (except in the `vars` definition itself). It is only available in Jinja contexts like models and macros.
  [+] B. `env_var()` reads system environment variables and works in `dbt_project.yml`; `var()` reads from `vars` and only works in Jinja
       -> Correct. `env_var()` reads system environment variables and is available in `dbt_project.yml`, `profiles.yml`, and Jinja code. `var()` reads from the `vars` configuration and is only available in Jinja contexts.
  [ ] C. `var()` can be used in `dbt_project.yml` to set default variable values; `env_var()` can only be used in model SQL files
       -> Incorrect. `env_var()` can be used in `dbt_project.yml` and `profiles.yml`, not just in model SQL. `var()` cannot be used in `dbt_project.yml`.
  [ ] D. `env_var()` and `var()` are interchangeable -- both read from the `vars` config in `dbt_project.yml`
       -> Incorrect. `env_var()` and `var()` are not interchangeable. `env_var()` reads OS environment variables while `var()` reads from the dbt `vars` config.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `var()` cannot be used in `dbt_project.yml` (except in the `vars` definition itself). It is only available in Jinja contexts like models and macros. - **B) Correct.** `env_var()` reads system environment variables and is available in `dbt_project.yml`, `profiles.yml`, and Jinja code. `var()` reads from the `vars` configuration and is only available in Jinja contexts. - **C) Incorrect.** `env_var()` can be used in `dbt_project.yml` and `profiles.yml`, not just in model SQL. `var()` cannot be used in `dbt_project.yml`. - **D) Incorrect.** `env_var()` and `var()` are not interchangeable. `env_var()` reads OS environment variables while `var()` reads from the dbt `vars` config. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/dbt-jinja-functions/env_var

Question 9 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A model `dim_hosts_cleansed` has an enforced contract with these column definitions: - name : host_id data_type : integer - name : host_name data_type : string - name : is_superhost data_type : string - name : updated_at data_type : timestamp - name : created_at data_type : timestamp The model's SELECT includes `NVL(host_name, 'Anonymous') AS host_name`. If a developer adds `LENGTH(host_name) AS name_length` without updating the YAML, what happens?

  [ ] A. The model builds successfully but the `name_length` column is silently dropped from the output
       -> Incorrect. Contracts do not silently drop extra columns. They enforce strict matching between output and the contract definition.
  [ ] B. dbt raises a compilation error before any SQL is executed
       -> Incorrect. The error occurs at execution time, not during compilation. dbt compares actual output columns against the contract after the SQL runs.
  [ ] C. The model builds but dbt issues a warning about the uncontracted column
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not issue a warning for contract violations. It raises an error because contracts are strict enforcement mechanisms.
  [+] D. dbt raises an error during execution because the column is not in the contract
       -> Correct. With `contract: {enforced: true}`, dbt validates that output columns match the YAML contract. A column not in the contract (`name_length`) causes an error at execution time.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Contracts do not silently drop extra columns. They enforce strict matching between output and the contract definition. - **B) Incorrect.** The error occurs at execution time, not during compilation. dbt compares actual output columns against the contract after the SQL runs. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt does not issue a warning for contract violations. It raises an error because contracts are strict enforcement mechanisms. - **D) Correct.** With `contract: {enforced: true}`, dbt validates that output columns match the YAML contract. A column not in the contract (`name_length`) causes an error at execution time. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-contracts#how-are-contracts-enforced

Question 10 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO statements about `is_incremental()` and `--full-refresh` are correct? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. `is_incremental()` returns `false` during a `--full-refresh` run
       -> Correct. `is_incremental()` returns `false` during a `--full-refresh` run, even if the target table exists, so the incremental filter is skipped.
  [ ] B. `is_incremental()` returns `true` during a `--full-refresh` run because the target table exists
       -> Incorrect. `is_incremental()` returns `false` during `--full-refresh`, not `true`. The flag explicitly overrides the existence check.
  [+] C. `--full-refresh` causes dbt to drop and recreate the target table from scratch
       -> Correct. `--full-refresh` causes dbt to drop and recreate the target table from scratch, loading all data without the incremental filter.
  [ ] D. `--full-refresh` only clears data but preserves the table structure (DDL)
       -> Incorrect. `--full-refresh` drops and recreates the entire table, not just the data. Both DDL and data are rebuilt.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `is_incremental()` returns `false` during a `--full-refresh` run, even if the target table exists, so the incremental filter is skipped. - **B) Incorrect.** `is_incremental()` returns `false` during `--full-refresh`, not `true`. The flag explicitly overrides the existence check. - **C) Correct.** `--full-refresh` causes dbt to drop and recreate the target table from scratch, loading all data without the incremental filter. - **D) Incorrect.** `--full-refresh` drops and recreates the entire table, not just the data. Both DDL and data are rebuilt. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/incremental-models#how-do-i-rebuild-an-incremental-model

Question 11 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A snapshot `scd_raw_listings` is configured with `strategy: timestamp` and `updated_at: updated_at`. A developer accidentally also adds `check_cols: ['name', 'price']`. What happens when `dbt snapshot` runs? snapshots : - name : scd_raw_listings relation : source ( 'airbnb' , 'listings' ) config : unique_key : id strategy : timestamp updated_at : updated_at check_cols : [ 'name' , 'price' ] hard_deletes : invalidate

  [ ] A. dbt uses both the timestamp strategy and monitors the specified check_cols for changes
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not combine strategies. When `strategy='timestamp'` is set, `check_cols` is irrelevant and not used alongside the timestamp logic.
  [ ] B. dbt raises a compilation error because you cannot specify check_cols with timestamp strategy
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not raise an error or warning for the extra `check_cols` config. It is silently ignored when the timestamp strategy is active.
  [+] C. dbt ignores check_cols and uses only the timestamp strategy
       -> Correct. When `strategy='timestamp'` is set, the `check_cols` configuration is silently ignored. dbt relies solely on the `updated_at` column to detect changes.
  [ ] D. dbt falls back to the check strategy because check_cols is explicitly provided
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not fall back to the check strategy. The `strategy` field explicitly controls which strategy is used, regardless of other configs present.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** dbt does not combine strategies. When `strategy='timestamp'` is set, `check_cols` is irrelevant and not used alongside the timestamp logic. - **B) Incorrect.** dbt does not raise an error or warning for the extra `check_cols` config. It is silently ignored when the timestamp strategy is active. - **C) Correct.** When `strategy='timestamp'` is set, the `check_cols` configuration is silently ignored. dbt relies solely on the `updated_at` column to detect changes. - **D) Incorrect.** dbt does not fall back to the check strategy. The `strategy` field explicitly controls which strategy is used, regardless of other configs present. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/snapshots#snapshot-configurations

Question 12 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A project has this post-hook and on-run-start configuration: # dbt_project.yml on - run - start : - "CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS {{ target.schema }}.audit_log (model_name STRING, run_timestamp TIMESTAMP)" models : airbnb : + post - hook : - "INSERT INTO {{ target.schema }}.audit_log VALUES ('{{ this }}', CURRENT_TIMESTAMP)" Model `fct_reviews` depends on `src_reviews`, which is ephemeral. What is the full execution order?

  [ ] A. Create audit_log -> Build src_reviews -> Post-hook src_reviews -> Build fct_reviews -> Post-hook fct_reviews
       -> Incorrect. Ephemeral models do not execute post-hooks because they never create a database object. There would be no post-hook for `src_reviews`.
  [ ] B. Build src_reviews -> Create audit_log -> Build fct_reviews -> Post-hook fct_reviews
       -> Incorrect. `on-run-start` hooks always run first, before any model execution, not between models.
  [ ] C. Create audit_log -> Build src_reviews -> Build fct_reviews -> Post-hook src_reviews -> Post-hook fct_reviews
       -> Incorrect. Ephemeral models do not have post-hooks executed because there is no `{{ this }}` relation for them.
  [+] D. Create audit_log -> Build fct_reviews with src_reviews inlined as a CTE -> Post-hook fct_reviews (no post-hook fires for the ephemeral model)
       -> Correct. The `on-run-start` hook runs first. Then dbt builds `fct_reviews` with `src_reviews` inlined as a CTE (since it is ephemeral). Because the ephemeral model never creates a database object, no post-hook fires for it -- only the post-hook for `fct_reviews` executes.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Ephemeral models do not execute post-hooks because they never create a database object. There would be no post-hook for `src_reviews`. - **B) Incorrect.** `on-run-start` hooks always run first, before any model execution, not between models. - **C) Incorrect.** Ephemeral models do not have post-hooks executed because there is no `{{ this }}` relation for them. - **D) Correct.** The `on-run-start` hook runs first. Then dbt builds `fct_reviews` with `src_reviews` inlined as a CTE (since it is ephemeral). Because the ephemeral model never creates a database object, no post-hook fires for it -- only the post-hook for `fct_reviews` executes. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-configs/pre-hook-post-hook

Question 13 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A staging model renames `price` to `price_str`, and a downstream cleansing model converts it: REPLACE(price_str, '$') :: NUMBER(10, 2) AS price If the source `price` column contains the value `'$1,234.56'` (with a comma), what happens?

  [ ] A. The value is correctly converted to `1234.56` because `REPLACE` removes the dollar sign and `::NUMBER` handles the comma
       -> Incorrect. `REPLACE` only removes the `$` character. It does not handle commas, so `::NUMBER` cannot parse the remaining string `'1,234.56'`.
  [+] B. The `REPLACE` removes only `$`, leaving `'1,234.56'`, and the `::NUMBER(10,2)` cast fails with a numeric conversion error
       -> Correct. `REPLACE(price_str, '$')` only removes the `$`, producing `'1,234.56'`. The `::NUMBER(10,2)` cast fails because the comma is not a valid numeric character.
  [ ] C. The value is converted to `1.23` because the comma truncates the number
       -> Incorrect. The comma does not truncate the number. It causes a conversion error because commas are not valid in numeric literals.
  [ ] D. dbt silently returns NULL for values it cannot convert
       -> Incorrect. The database does not silently return NULL for conversion errors. It raises a numeric conversion error.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `REPLACE` only removes the `$` character. It does not handle commas, so `::NUMBER` cannot parse the remaining string `'1,234.56'`. - **B) Correct.** `REPLACE(price_str, '$')` only removes the `$`, producing `'1,234.56'`. The `::NUMBER(10,2)` cast fails because the comma is not a valid numeric character. - **C) Incorrect.** The comma does not truncate the number. It causes a conversion error because commas are not valid in numeric literals. - **D) Incorrect.** The database does not silently return NULL for conversion errors. It raises a numeric conversion error. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/sql-models

Question 14 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A model uses `dbt_utils.generate_surrogate_key`: {{ dbt_utils.generate_surrogate_key(['listing_id', 'review_date', 'reviewer_name', 'review_text']) }} as review_id What does it produce, and what happens if `reviewer_name` is NULL?

  [+] A. It generates an MD5 hash; NULL values are replaced with a placeholder string before hashing, so the key is still deterministic
       -> Correct. `generate_surrogate_key` produces an MD5 hash of concatenated column values. NULL values are replaced with a placeholder string (`'_dbt_utils_surrogate_key_null_'`) before hashing, ensuring a deterministic, non-null hash.
  [ ] B. It generates an MD5 hash of the concatenated column values; NULL columns cause the entire hash to be NULL
       -> Incorrect. NULL columns do not cause the entire hash to be NULL. The macro replaces NULLs with a placeholder string before concatenation and hashing.
  [ ] C. It generates an auto-incrementing integer; NULL values are ignored
       -> Incorrect. `generate_surrogate_key` produces an MD5 hash, not an auto-incrementing integer. It is deterministic based on input values.
  [ ] D. It generates a UUID that is random on each run; NULL values do not affect the output
       -> Incorrect. `generate_surrogate_key` produces a deterministic MD5 hash, not a random UUID. The same inputs always produce the same hash.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `generate_surrogate_key` produces an MD5 hash of concatenated column values. NULL values are replaced with a placeholder string (`'_dbt_utils_surrogate_key_null_'`) before hashing, ensuring a deterministic, non-null hash. - **B) Incorrect.** NULL columns do not cause the entire hash to be NULL. The macro replaces NULLs with a placeholder string before concatenation and hashing. - **C) Incorrect.** `generate_surrogate_key` produces an MD5 hash, not an auto-incrementing integer. It is deterministic based on input values. - **D) Incorrect.** `generate_surrogate_key` produces a deterministic MD5 hash, not a random UUID. The same inputs always produce the same hash. Reference: https://github.com/dbt-labs/dbt-utils#generate_surrogate_key

Question 15 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A CSV file called `seed_full_moon_dates.csv` sits in the project's `seeds/` directory and is referenced by a mart model using `{{ ref('seed_full_moon_dates') }}`. Which dbt command loads this CSV into the data warehouse?

  [ ] A. `dbt run --select seed_full_moon_dates`
       -> Incorrect. `dbt run` only executes models, not seeds. Seeds require the `dbt seed` command.
  [+] B. `dbt seed` (loads all CSV seeds)
       -> Correct. `dbt seed` reads CSV files from the `seeds/` directory and loads them as tables in the warehouse.
  [ ] C. `dbt source load --seeds`
       -> Incorrect. `dbt source load --seeds` is not a valid dbt command.
  [ ] D. `dbt build --resource-type seed`
       -> Incorrect. While `dbt build --resource-type seed` is valid syntax, `dbt seed` is the dedicated and canonical command for loading seeds.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `dbt run` only executes models, not seeds. Seeds require the `dbt seed` command. - **B) Correct.** `dbt seed` reads CSV files from the `seeds/` directory and loads them as tables in the warehouse. - **C) Incorrect.** `dbt source load --seeds` is not a valid dbt command. - **D) Incorrect.** While `dbt build --resource-type seed` is valid syntax, `dbt seed` is the dedicated and canonical command for loading seeds. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/seeds

Question 16 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What is the correct Jinja syntax for a comment that will NOT appear in the compiled SQL?

  [ ] A. `/* Filter out empty strings */`
       -> Incorrect. `/* */` is a SQL block comment that passes through to the compiled SQL output.
  [ ] B. `-- Filter out empty strings`
       -> Incorrect. `--` is a SQL line comment that also passes through to the compiled SQL output.
  [+] C. `{# Filter out empty strings #}`
       -> Correct. Jinja comments use `{# ... #}` and are stripped during compilation, so they never appear in compiled SQL.
  [ ] D. `{{ "Filter out empty strings" }}`
       -> Incorrect. `{{ }}` is a Jinja expression delimiter that outputs the enclosed value as part of the SQL.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `/* */` is a SQL block comment that passes through to the compiled SQL output. - **B) Incorrect.** `--` is a SQL line comment that also passes through to the compiled SQL output. - **C) Correct.** Jinja comments use `{# ... #}` and are stripped during compilation, so they never appear in compiled SQL. - **D) Incorrect.** `{{ }}` is a Jinja expression delimiter that outputs the enclosed value as part of the SQL. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/jinja-macros#jinja

Question 18 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
An incremental model contains this block: {% if is_incremental () %} AND review_date > ( select max ( review_date ) from {{ this }}) {% endif %} What does `{{ this }}` refer to?

  [ ] A. The source table that feeds into this model
       -> Incorrect. `{{ this }}` does not refer to source tables. To reference sources, you use the `source()` function.
  [+] B. The current model's already-existing database table from previous runs
       -> Correct. In an incremental model, `{{ this }}` resolves to the existing database relation (table) created by previous runs. It is commonly used to find the maximum watermark value so only newer rows are processed.
  [ ] C. A temporary staging table created during the current run
       -> Incorrect. `{{ this }}` does not refer to a temporary staging table -- it points to the persisted table from prior runs.
  [ ] D. The compiled SQL query of the current model
       -> Incorrect. `{{ this }}` resolves to a database relation name, not to the compiled SQL query itself.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `{{ this }}` does not refer to source tables. To reference sources, you use the `source()` function. - **B) Correct.** In an incremental model, `{{ this }}` resolves to the existing database relation (table) created by previous runs. It is commonly used to find the maximum watermark value so only newer rows are processed. - **C) Incorrect.** `{{ this }}` does not refer to a temporary staging table -- it points to the persisted table from prior runs. - **D) Incorrect.** `{{ this }}` resolves to a database relation name, not to the compiled SQL query itself. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/dbt-jinja-functions/this

  [ ] A. It defines a legal agreement between data producers and consumers about the model's expected output schema
       -> Incorrect. A model contract is a technical enforcement mechanism in dbt, not a legal agreement.
  [+] B. It enforces that the model's output must have exactly these columns with these data types -- any deviation causes a build error
       -> Correct. When `contract: {enforced: true}` is set, dbt validates that the model output matches the contract exactly -- column names, count, and data types. Any deviation causes a build failure.
  [ ] C. It prevents any changes to the model's SQL code without peer review approval through dbt Cloud governance
       -> Incorrect. Contracts do not control code review processes -- they enforce output schema guarantees at build time.
  [ ] D. It locks the model's materialization strategy and target schema so neither can be changed after deployment
       -> Incorrect. Contracts enforce column structure, not materialization settings. Materialization can still be changed independently.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** A model contract is a technical enforcement mechanism in dbt, not a legal agreement. - **B) Correct.** When `contract: {enforced: true}` is set, dbt validates that the model output matches the contract exactly -- column names, count, and data types. Any deviation causes a build failure. - **C) Incorrect.** Contracts do not control code review processes -- they enforce output schema guarantees at build time. - **D) Incorrect.** Contracts enforce column structure, not materialization settings. Materialization can still be changed independently. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-contracts

Question 20 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
You set `deprecation_date: 2026-01-01` on the v1 definition of `dim_listings_cleansed`. What is the effect of this configuration?

  [ ] A. After that date, `dbt run` skips the model and it is no longer built
       -> Incorrect. `deprecation_date` does not stop the model from building. It signals an intended sunset date, not an execution cutoff.
  [+] B. dbt emits a deprecation warning when the model is built or referenced, but the model still builds normally
       -> Correct. A `deprecation_date` makes dbt emit warnings -- to the producer when the model is built, and to any model that `ref()`s it -- so teams have a window to migrate. The model keeps building.
  [ ] C. dbt drops the model from the warehouse automatically once the date passes
       -> Incorrect. dbt never drops the relation on a deprecation date; removing the model is a manual decision left to the team.
  [ ] D. The model becomes read-only, so downstream models can no longer `ref()` it
       -> Incorrect. Deprecation does not make a model read-only or block `ref()`. References keep working and simply raise a warning.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `deprecation_date` does not stop the model from building. It signals an intended sunset date, not an execution cutoff. - **B) Correct.** A `deprecation_date` makes dbt emit warnings -- to the producer when the model is built, and to any model that `ref()`s it -- so teams have a window to migrate. The model keeps building. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt never drops the relation on a deprecation date; removing the model is a manual decision left to the team. - **D) Incorrect.** Deprecation does not make a model read-only or block `ref()`. References keep working and simply raise a warning. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-properties/deprecation_date

Question 21 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
A dbt model defines column-level constraints under an enforced contract (`contract: {enforced: true}`) on Snowflake. Which TWO statements about how these constraints behave are TRUE? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. `not_null` constraints are enforced by the warehouse when the model is built
       -> Correct. `not_null` is the one constraint the major cloud warehouses (Snowflake, BigQuery, Redshift) actually enforce at build time -- a null in that column fails the build.
  [ ] B. `check` constraints are enforced by Snowflake when the model is built
       -> Incorrect. Snowflake does not support the `check` syntax; dbt skips the `check` config and raises a warning rather than enforcing it.
  [+] C. `primary_key` and `unique` constraints are accepted but treated as metadata only -- the warehouse still admits duplicate values
       -> Correct. On Snowflake, `primary_key` and `unique` are informational only. dbt records them as metadata, but the warehouse still admits duplicate values.
  [ ] D. Constraints take effect even without setting `contract: enforced: true`
       -> Incorrect. Constraint DDL is only emitted when the model has `contract: enforced: true`. Without an enforced contract, dbt does not apply the constraints at all.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `not_null` is the one constraint the major cloud warehouses (Snowflake, BigQuery, Redshift) actually enforce at build time -- a null in that column fails the build. - **B) Incorrect.** Snowflake does not support the `check` syntax; dbt skips the `check` config and raises a warning rather than enforcing it. - **C) Correct.** On Snowflake, `primary_key` and `unique` are informational only. dbt records them as metadata, but the warehouse still admits duplicate values. - **D) Incorrect.** Constraint DDL is only emitted when the model has `contract: enforced: true`. Without an enforced contract, dbt does not apply the constraints at all. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-properties/constraints

Question 22 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A model `fct_orders` is configured as follows: {{ config ( materialized = 'incremental' , incremental_strategy = 'microbatch' , event_time = 'created_at' , begin = '2024-01-01' , batch_size = 'day' , lookback = 3 ) }} select * from {{ source ( 'raw' , 'orders' ) }} Today is 2026-05-26 and the target table does not yet exist in the warehouse. The developer runs `dbt run --select fct_orders` without any `--event-time-start` / `--event-time-end` flags. The source contains rows for every day since 2024-01-01. How does dbt execute this run?

  [ ] A. One batch — dbt builds the model with all rows from `begin` to today in a single statement, because `lookback` only applies on subsequent incremental runs
       -> Incorrect. Microbatch never executes the full window in one statement. The whole point of microbatch is that dbt splits the range into independent, idempotent `batch_size` batches that can be retried in isolation.
  [ ] B. 4 batches — only the current day plus the 3 lookback days, because `begin` is ignored when no `--event-time-start` is provided
       -> Incorrect. `begin` is not ignored. On the first run (table doesn't exist), dbt processes every batch from `begin` through "now." `lookback` only controls what gets reprocessed on subsequent runs.
  [+] C. ~877 batches — one per day from `begin='2024-01-01'` through 2026-05-26, because on the first run dbt backfills every day in the `[begin, now]` window; subsequent runs would process only 4 batches (today + lookback=3)
       -> Correct. On the initial run dbt backfills the `[begin, now]` window one `batch_size` period at a time — 2024-01-01 → 2026-05-26 inclusive is roughly 877 daily batches. On every subsequent run, dbt processes only the current period plus `lookback` prior periods (here, 4 daily batches).
  [ ] D. The run fails at compile time because microbatch models require explicit `--event-time-start` and `--event-time-end` flags on the first invocation
       -> Incorrect. `--event-time-start` / `--event-time-end` are optional overrides for explicit backfills. Without them, dbt derives the window from `begin` and the current timestamp.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Microbatch never executes the full window in one statement. The whole point of microbatch is that dbt splits the range into independent, idempotent `batch_size` batches that can be retried in isolation. - **B) Incorrect.** `begin` is not ignored. On the first run (table doesn't exist), dbt processes every batch from `begin` through "now." `lookback` only controls what gets reprocessed on subsequent runs. - **C) Correct.** On the initial run dbt backfills the `[begin, now]` window one `batch_size` period at a time — 2024-01-01 → 2026-05-26 inclusive is roughly 877 daily batches. On every subsequent run, dbt processes only the current period plus `lookback` prior periods (here, 4 daily batches). - **D) Incorrect.** `--event-time-start` / `--event-time-end` are optional overrides for explicit backfills. Without them, dbt derives the window from `begin` and the current timestamp. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/incremental-microbatch

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Question 23 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A team upgrades from dbt Core 1.7 to 1.11. After the upgrade, `dbt parse` emits deprecation warnings every run about packages overriding built-in materializations. To keep the previous (1.7) behavior while the team plans a fix, an engineer adds the following to `dbt_project.yml`: flags: require_explicit_package_overrides_for_builtin_materializations: False What is the effect of this configuration?

  [ ] A. It enables the new v1.11 strict behavior — implicit overrides now raise an error at parse time, helping the team find every package that needs an explicit opt-in
       -> Incorrect. The strict, error-raising behavior is what `True` does. Setting the flag to `False` does the opposite — it preserves the old permissive behavior.
  [+] B. It opts out of the new v1.11 behavior change and preserves the legacy permissive behavior, so installed packages can continue to silently override built-in materializations without warning
       -> Correct. `require_explicit_package_overrides_for_builtin_materializations` is a behavior-change flag introduced in v1.11. Setting it to `False` opts out of the new strict default and restores 1.7-style silent overrides, which silences the deprecation warning. Behavior-change flags exist precisely to let teams migrate at their own pace.
  [ ] C. It increases the log verbosity so every package that overrides a built-in materialization is logged at INFO level, but does not change the override semantics
       -> Incorrect. Behavior flags change semantics, not logging verbosity. Logging is controlled separately (e.g. `--log-level`).
  [ ] D. It tells dbt to refuse to load any third-party packages until each is explicitly listed in a new `package_overrides:` block, effectively quarantining the project from packages
       -> Incorrect. No `package_overrides:` block exists in dbt. Packages continue to load normally regardless of this flag's value.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The strict, error-raising behavior is what `True` does. Setting the flag to `False` does the opposite — it preserves the old permissive behavior. - **B) Correct.** `require_explicit_package_overrides_for_builtin_materializations` is a behavior-change flag introduced in v1.11. Setting it to `False` opts out of the new strict default and restores 1.7-style silent overrides, which silences the deprecation warning. Behavior-change flags exist precisely to let teams migrate at their own pace. - **C) Incorrect.** Behavior flags change semantics, not logging verbosity. Logging is controlled separately (e.g. `--log-level`). - **D) Incorrect.** No `package_overrides:` block exists in dbt. Packages continue to load normally regardless of this flag's value. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/global-configs/behavior-changes

       -> Incorrect. dbt does not write compiled SQL to the `logs/` directory -- logs contain runtime debug information.
  [ ] B. `target/run/airbnb/dim_listings_cleansed.compiled.sql`
       -> Incorrect. The path format `target/run/.../compiled.sql` is not correct. Compiled SQL uses the `target/compiled/` directory.

       -> Incorrect. There is no `build/` directory in a standard dbt project structure.

       -> Correct. dbt writes compiled SQL (with all Jinja resolved) to the `target/compiled/` directory, mirroring the model's project path.

Explanation:

Compiled SQL uses the `target/compiled/` directory. - **C) Incorrect.** There is no `build/` directory in a standard dbt project structure. - **D) Correct.** dbt writes compiled SQL (with all Jinja resolved) to the `target/compiled/` directory, mirroring the model's project path. Question 26 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What type of error does dbt report when the Jinja compiles successfully but the database rejects the resulting SQL?

  [+] A. Database Error
       -> Correct. A Database Error occurs when dbt successfully compiles Jinja/SQL but the database engine rejects the query (e.g., invalid column, missing table, SQL syntax error).
  [ ] B. Compilation Error
       -> Incorrect. Compilation Errors happen during Jinja/SQL compilation, before any SQL reaches the database.
  [ ] C. Dependency Error
       -> Incorrect. Dependency Errors occur when a referenced model or source cannot be found in the project.
  [ ] D. Configuration Error
       -> Incorrect. Configuration Errors relate to invalid project or profile settings, not database-level SQL rejections.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** A Database Error occurs when dbt successfully compiles Jinja/SQL but the database engine rejects the query (e.g., invalid column, missing table, SQL syntax error). - **B) Incorrect.** Compilation Errors happen during Jinja/SQL compilation, before any SQL reaches the database. - **C) Incorrect.** Dependency Errors occur when a referenced model or source cannot be found in the project. - **D) Incorrect.** Configuration Errors relate to invalid project or profile settings, not database-level SQL rejections. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/guides/debug-errors#types-of-errors

  [+] A. Running the model with `--full-refresh` to determine whether the error is specific to incremental logic
       -> Correct. Running `--full-refresh` bypasses incremental logic, helping isolate whether the error is specific to the incremental path.
  [+] B. Inspecting `target/compiled/` to verify whether the `is_incremental()` block was included in the compiled SQL
       -> Correct. Inspecting `target/compiled/` reveals whether the `is_incremental()` block was included, confirming if the incremental filter was applied.

  [ ] D. Converting the model to a seed file and reloading the data as a CSV to bypass the schema change
       -> Incorrect. Converting a model to a seed is not a debugging approach -- it fundamentally changes the resource type and bypasses the actual issue.

Type: MULTIPLE
You run `dbt run -s dim_listings` and get: `Relation "dev_zoltan"."src_listings" does not exist`. Which TWO are possible causes? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. The src_listings model has never been run before and does not exist in the warehouse
       -> Correct. If the model has never been run, the table/view does not exist in the warehouse, causing a relation-not-found error.
  [ ] B. The model is defined as ephemeral and never creates a database object
       -> Incorrect. Ephemeral models are injected as CTEs and would produce a different error pattern, not a relation-not-found error.

       -> Correct. If the model uses a custom schema, the reference may resolve to the wrong schema location (e.g., `dev_zoltan_staging` instead of `dev_zoltan`).
  [ ] D. The model is a Python model that has not been compiled yet
       -> Incorrect. There is no separate compilation step for Python models that would cause this error. Python models compile and execute in one step.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** If the model has never been run, the table/view does not exist in the warehouse, causing a relation-not-found error. - **B) Incorrect.** Ephemeral models are injected as CTEs and would produce a different error pattern, not a relation-not-found error. - **C) Correct.** If the model uses a custom schema, the reference may resolve to the wrong schema location (e.g., `dev_zoltan_staging` instead of `dev_zoltan`). - **D) Incorrect.** There is no separate compilation step for Python models that would cause this error. Python models compile and execute in one step. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/custom-schemas

Question 30 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A developer encounters a compilation error with this Jinja code: {% set room_types = [ 'Entire home/apt' , 'Private room' , 'Shared room' , 'Hotel room' ] %} {% for rt in room_types %} {% if rt == 'Hotel room' %} {% set found = true %} {% endfor %} What is the root cause?

  [ ] A. `{% set found = true %}` is not valid Jinja syntax
       -> Incorrect. `{% set found = true %}` is valid Jinja syntax for variable assignment.
  [+] B. The `{% if %}` block is not closed before `{% endfor %}`
       -> Correct. The `{% if %}` block is opened but never closed with `{% endif %}` before the `{% endfor %}`. Jinja block tags must be properly nested.
  [ ] C. You cannot use `{% set %}` inside a `{% for %}` loop
       -> Incorrect. `{% set %}` can be used inside `{% for %}` loops. This is valid Jinja syntax.
  [ ] D. The `room_types` list uses incorrect Jinja syntax
       -> Incorrect. The `room_types` list uses correct Jinja/Python list syntax with string literals.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `{% set found = true %}` is valid Jinja syntax for variable assignment. - **B) Correct.** The `{% if %}` block is opened but never closed with `{% endif %}` before the `{% endfor %}`. Jinja block tags must be properly nested. - **C) Incorrect.** `{% set %}` can be used inside `{% for %}` loops. This is valid Jinja syntax. - **D) Incorrect.** The `room_types` list uses correct Jinja/Python list syntax with string literals. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/jinja-macros#jinja-basics

Question 31 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
You run `dbt run --select fct_reviews` and get a database error that the SQL is invalid. Which TWO approaches help debug the compiled SQL? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. Run `dbt compile --select fct_reviews` and inspect `target/compiled/`
       -> Correct. `dbt compile --select fct_reviews` renders all Jinja and writes the compiled SQL to `target/compiled/`, allowing you to inspect the pure SQL.
  [+] B. Check `target/run/` for the exact SQL sent to the warehouse
       -> Correct. `target/run/` contains the actual executed SQL including the DDL wrapper (CREATE TABLE AS, etc.), showing exactly what was sent to the warehouse.
  [ ] C. Run `dbt debug` to see the compiled SQL output
       -> Incorrect. `dbt debug` tests your database connection and configuration, not model compilation. It does not show compiled SQL.
  [ ] D. Check `target/manifest.json` which contains the fully compiled SQL
       -> Incorrect. While `manifest.json` does contain compiled code, the `target/compiled/` and `target/run/` directories provide SQL in directly usable `.sql` files, making them the practical choice for debugging.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `dbt compile --select fct_reviews` renders all Jinja and writes the compiled SQL to `target/compiled/`, allowing you to inspect the pure SQL. - **B) Correct.** `target/run/` contains the actual executed SQL including the DDL wrapper (CREATE TABLE AS, etc.), showing exactly what was sent to the warehouse. - **C) Incorrect.** `dbt debug` tests your database connection and configuration, not model compilation. It does not show compiled SQL. - **D) Incorrect.** While `manifest.json` does contain compiled code, the `target/compiled/` and `target/run/` directories provide SQL in directly usable `.sql` files, making them the practical choice for debugging. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/commands/compile

Type: MULTIPLE
Select two best practices for managing production pipeline failures. (Choose 2)

  [+] A. Using `dbt retry` to rerun only the failed and skipped nodes after fixing the root cause
       -> Correct. Best practice is to diagnose the issue, fix it, and use `dbt retry` to rerun only the failed and skipped nodes.
  [ ] B. Always running `dbt run --full-refresh` on all models after any failure
       -> Incorrect. Running `--full-refresh` on all models after every failure is wasteful and unnecessary.
  [+] C. Configuring alerting on job failures so the team is notified promptly
       -> Correct. Configuring alerting on job failures ensures the team is notified promptly and can respond quickly.
  [ ] D. Dropping and recreating all downstream tables after every failure
       -> Incorrect. Dropping and recreating all downstream tables is destructive and disproportionate to most failures.

Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/commands/retry

Question 34 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A DAG has: `src_listings -> dim_listings_cleansed -> dim_listings_w_hosts -> mart_fullmoon_reviews` and `src_reviews -> fct_reviews -> mart_fullmoon_reviews`. With `--threads 8`, what is the minimum number of sequential "rounds" to build the entire project?

  [ ] A. 2 rounds because there are 2 parallel branches
       -> Incorrect. The number of parallel branches does not determine the number of sequential rounds. The critical path length determines the minimum.
  [ ] B. 5 rounds because every model must wait for all its dependencies before it can build
       -> Incorrect. While models do wait for their dependencies, the minimum number of rounds equals the length of the longest dependency chain (the critical path), not total nodes. Parallel branches reduce rounds, not increase them.
  [ ] C. 8 rounds because of the thread count
       -> Incorrect. The thread count sets the maximum parallelism but does not determine the minimum number of rounds. That is determined by the critical path.
  [+] D. 4 rounds because the longest chain has 4 sequential models
       -> Correct. The minimum sequential steps equals the critical path (longest dependency chain): `src_listings -> dim_listings_cleansed -> dim_listings_w_hosts -> mart_fullmoon_reviews` (4 steps).

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The number of parallel branches does not determine the number of sequential rounds. The critical path length determines the minimum. - **B) Incorrect.** While models do wait for their dependencies, the minimum number of rounds equals the length of the longest dependency chain (the critical path), not total nodes. Parallel branches reduce rounds, not increase them. - **C) Incorrect.** The thread count sets the maximum parallelism but does not determine the minimum number of rounds. That is determined by the critical path. - **D) Correct.** The minimum sequential steps equals the critical path (longest dependency chain): `src_listings -> dim_listings_cleansed -> dim_listings_w_hosts -> mart_fullmoon_reviews` (4 steps). Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/running-a-dbt-project/using-threads

       -> Correct. Line 2 has no `info=True` (log file only). Line 3 has `info=True` (screen output). Line 4 uses a SQL comment but Jinja still executes the `log()` (screen output). Line 5 is a Jinja comment and is completely ignored. Two messages appear.
  [ ] D. 0 messages -- `log()` only writes to the log file, never the screen
       -> Incorrect. `log()` with `info=True` does print to the terminal screen, not just the log file.

Explanation:

Line 4 uses a SQL comment (`--`), but Jinja processes before SQL rendering, so the `log()` on that line still executes. - **C) Correct.** Line 2 has no `info=True` (log file only). Line 3 has `info=True` (screen output). Line 4 uses a SQL comment but Jinja still executes the `log()` (screen output). Line 5 is a Jinja comment and is completely ignored. Question 36 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What is the purpose of `dbt build` compared to running `dbt run` and `dbt test` separately?

  [+] A. `dbt build` runs models and tests in DAG order, testing each model immediately after it is built
       -> Correct. `dbt build` executes nodes in DAG order, interleaving model runs and tests. After a model is built, its tests run immediately, and downstream models only execute if tests pass.
  [ ] B. `dbt build` is an alias for `dbt run && dbt test` with no behavioral difference at all
       -> Incorrect. `dbt build` is not just an alias. It interleaves tests with model runs in DAG order, unlike running `dbt run && dbt test` which runs all models first, then all tests.
  [ ] C. `dbt build` runs all tests first to validate data, then builds all models afterward
       -> Incorrect. `dbt build` does not run all tests first. It interleaves tests with model runs in dependency order.
  [ ] D. `dbt build` only builds models that have tests defined in their YAML properties
       -> Incorrect. `dbt build` builds all selected models, not just those with tests defined. It also processes seeds and snapshots.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `dbt build` executes nodes in DAG order, interleaving model runs and tests. After a model is built, its tests run immediately, and downstream models only execute if tests pass. - **B) Incorrect.** `dbt build` is not just an alias. It interleaves tests with model runs in DAG order, unlike running `dbt run && dbt test` which runs all models first, then all tests. - **C) Incorrect.** `dbt build` does not run all tests first. It interleaves tests with model runs in dependency order. - **D) Incorrect.** `dbt build` builds all selected models, not just those with tests defined. It also processes seeds and snapshots. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/commands/build

       -> Correct. `dbt retry` reads the `run_results.json` artifact to identify which nodes failed or were skipped, then re-executes only those nodes.

       -> Incorrect. `dbt retry` does not rerun all models -- it only reruns failed and skipped nodes from the most recent invocation.

       -> Incorrect. `dbt retry` does not retry database connections -- it re-executes specific failed nodes.
  [ ] D. It rolls back the failed models to their previous state in the warehouse
       -> Incorrect. `dbt retry` does not roll back models -- it re-executes them to produce updated results.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `dbt retry` reads the `run_results.json` artifact to identify which nodes failed or were skipped, then re-executes only those nodes. - **B) Incorrect.** `dbt retry` does not rerun all models -- it only reruns failed and skipped nodes from the most recent invocation. - **C) Incorrect.** `dbt retry` does not retry database connections -- it re-executes specific failed nodes. - **D) Incorrect.** `dbt retry` does not roll back models -- it re-executes them to produce updated results.   [ ] A. A compressed backup of the entire database schema stored in the warehouse
       -> Incorrect. A zero-copy clone is not a compressed backup -- it creates a lightweight reference to existing data.
  [ ] B. A dbt command that duplicates a project's YAML configuration files locally
       -> Incorrect. `dbt clone` clones database relations, not YAML configuration files.
  [+] C. A database-level clone that creates a new reference to existing data without physically copying it
       -> Correct. `dbt clone` leverages the data platform's zero-copy cloning capability (e.g., on Snowflake) to create a new relation that points to the same underlying storage without duplicating data.
  [ ] D. A Git operation that clones the dbt repository without any commit history
       -> Incorrect. `dbt clone` is a dbt command for database operations, not a Git clone operation.

Explanation:

  [+] A. The `accepted_values` test will fail because `'Studio'` is not in the allowed list
       -> Correct. The `accepted_values` test checks that every non-null value in the column is within the provided list. Since `'Studio'` is not listed, the test fails.
  [ ] B. The test will pass because `accepted_values` only checks for NULL values
       -> Incorrect. `accepted_values` checks actual values against the allowed list, not just for NULLs. That is the `not_null` test.
  [ ] C. dbt will automatically add `'Studio'` to the accepted values list
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not auto-modify test configurations -- the test simply fails when an unlisted value is found.
  [ ] D. The model will fail to compile due to the unrecognized value
       -> Incorrect. The test runs after the model builds successfully -- unrecognized values do not cause compilation errors.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** The `accepted_values` test checks that every non-null value in the column is within the provided list. Since `'Studio'` is not listed, the test fails. - **B) Incorrect.** `accepted_values` checks actual values against the allowed list, not just for NULLs. That is the `not_null` test. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt does not auto-modify test configurations -- the test simply fails when an unlisted value is found. - **D) Incorrect.** The test runs after the model builds successfully -- unrecognized values do not cause compilation errors. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-properties/data-tests#accepted_values

       -> Incorrect. The `not_null` test checks for NULL values in a column.

       -> Correct. The `relationships` test verifies referential integrity by checking that every value in one column exists in a column of another model. It is configured with `to: ref('target_model')` and `field: column_name`.

       -> Incorrect. The `accepted_values` test checks that values are within a defined set.

Question 46 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A dbt project defines a model with three versions: models : - name : dim_listings latest_version : 2 versions : - v : 1 - v : 2 - v : 3 Another model references it using `{{ ref('dim_listings') }}` without specifying a version. Which version does this resolve to?

  [ ] A. Version 1, because it is the earliest stable version
       -> Incorrect. The earliest version is not automatically the default. `latest_version` explicitly controls which version unversioned `ref()` calls resolve to.
  [+] B. Version 2, because `latest_version: 2` makes it the default for unversioned refs
       -> Correct. When `latest_version: 2` is set, any `ref('dim_listings')` without a version argument resolves to `v2`. This allows gradual migration: consumers can stay on older versions while a newer one is developed.
  [ ] C. Version 3, because dbt always defaults to the most recently defined version
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not automatically default to the most recently defined version. The `latest_version` key is required to set the default.
  [ ] D. dbt raises an error because an unversioned `ref()` is ambiguous when multiple versions exist
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not error on unversioned refs when `latest_version` is set. It resolves cleanly to the version specified in `latest_version`.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The earliest version is not automatically the default. `latest_version` explicitly controls which version unversioned `ref()` calls resolve to. - **B) Correct.** When `latest_version: 2` is set, any `ref('dim_listings')` without a version argument resolves to `v2`. This allows gradual migration: consumers can stay on older versions while a newer one is developed. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt does not automatically default to the most recently defined version. The `latest_version` key is required to set the default. - **D) Incorrect.** dbt does not error on unversioned refs when `latest_version` is set. It resolves cleanly to the version specified in `latest_version`. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-versions

Question 56 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO statements about dbt packages are correct? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. Packages are installed by running `dbt deps` and stored in the `dbt_packages/` directory
       -> Correct. Packages are installed via `dbt deps` into the `dbt_packages/` directory, which is typically gitignored.
  [ ] B. Package versions are locked in `package-lock.yml` after the first install and never change
       -> Incorrect. While `package-lock.yml` records resolved versions, packages are re-resolved on each `dbt deps` run if the lock file is deleted or version ranges change.
  [+] C. You can reference macros from installed packages using the `package_name.macro_name` syntax (e.g., `dbt_utils.generate_surrogate_key`)
       -> Correct. Package macros are referenced using the `package_name.macro_name` namespace syntax, such as `dbt_utils.generate_surrogate_key`.
  [ ] D. Packages are automatically installed when you run `dbt run`
       -> Incorrect. `dbt run` does not automatically install packages. You must run `dbt deps` separately before running models.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Packages are installed via `dbt deps` into the `dbt_packages/` directory, which is typically gitignored. - **B) Incorrect.** While `package-lock.yml` records resolved versions, packages are re-resolved on each `dbt deps` run if the lock file is deleted or version ranges change. - **C) Correct.** Package macros are referenced using the `package_name.macro_name` namespace syntax, such as `dbt_utils.generate_surrogate_key`. - **D) Incorrect.** `dbt run` does not automatically install packages. You must run `dbt deps` separately before running models. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/packages

       -> Correct. Exposures are YAML-defined declarations of downstream consumers of your dbt models, such as dashboards, applications, or ML models. They appear in the DAG and documentation.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** An exposure is not a security vulnerability -- it is a documentation and lineage feature in dbt. - **B) Incorrect.** Exposures do not publish metadata to external APIs or data catalogs -- they document dependencies within the dbt project. - **C) Incorrect.** A model with `access: public` is a model governance concept, not an exposure. Exposures represent downstream consumers of models. - **D) Correct.** Exposures are YAML-defined declarations of downstream consumers of your dbt models, such as dashboards, applications, or ML models. They appear in the DAG and documentation. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/exposures

Question 59 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Select two valid methods for combining selectors in dbt. (Choose 2)

  [+] A. A space indicates union (OR): `dbt run --select model_a model_b`
       -> Correct. A space between selectors creates a union (OR) -- nodes matching either selector are included.
  [+] B. A comma indicates intersection (AND): `dbt run --select tag:nightly,state:modified`
       -> Correct. A comma creates an intersection (AND) -- only nodes matching both selectors are included. For example, `tag:nightly,state:modified` selects models that are both tagged "nightly" AND state-modified.
  [ ] C. The `&` symbol indicates intersection: `dbt run --select model_a & model_b`
       -> Incorrect. The `&` symbol is not a valid dbt selector operator. Use a comma for intersection.
  [ ] D. The `|` symbol indicates union: `dbt run --select model_a | model_b`
       -> Incorrect. The `|` symbol is not a valid dbt selector operator. Use a space for union.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** A space between selectors creates a union (OR) -- nodes matching either selector are included. - **B) Correct.** A comma creates an intersection (AND) -- only nodes matching both selectors are included. For example, `tag:nightly,state:modified` selects models that are both tagged "nightly" AND state-modified. - **C) Incorrect.** The `&` symbol is not a valid dbt selector operator. Use a comma for intersection. - **D) Incorrect.** The `|` symbol is not a valid dbt selector operator. Use a space for union. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/set-operators

Question 60 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What is the typical Slim CI workflow for testing changes in a pull request?

  [+] A. Run `dbt build --select state:modified+ --defer --state prod-artifacts/` to build changed models and dependents in a CI schema
       -> Correct. The standard Slim CI workflow uses `state:modified+` to select changed models and their downstream dependents, `--defer` to resolve references to unmodified models from production, and `--state` to point to the production manifest.
  [ ] B. Run `dbt build` on the entire project in a dedicated CI schema to rebuild everything from scratch
       -> Incorrect. Running `dbt build` on the entire project in CI is wasteful -- Slim CI specifically avoids rebuilding everything from scratch.
  [ ] C. Run `dbt test` on changed models without building them first, relying on stale warehouse data
       -> Incorrect. Running only tests without building the changed models first would test stale warehouse data, not the current changes.
  [ ] D. Run `dbt compile` to verify SQL validity without executing any models or tests
       -> Incorrect. `dbt compile` only validates SQL compilation -- it does not execute any models or tests, so it cannot catch runtime issues.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** The standard Slim CI workflow uses `state:modified+` to select changed models and their downstream dependents, `--defer` to resolve references to unmodified models from production, and `--state` to point to the production manifest. - **B) Incorrect.** Running `dbt build` on the entire project in CI is wasteful -- Slim CI specifically avoids rebuilding everything from scratch. - **C) Incorrect.** Running only tests without building the changed models first would test stale warehouse data, not the current changes. - **D) Incorrect.** `dbt compile` only validates SQL compilation -- it does not execute any models or tests, so it cannot catch runtime issues. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/deploy/continuous-integration

       -> Incorrect. `state:new` only selects newly added models, not modified existing models. It also lacks the `+` operator for downstream dependents and the `--defer` flag.

It also lacks the `+` operator for downstream dependents and the `--defer` flag. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/deploy/continuous-integration

  [+] C. dbt inlines `src_reviews` as a CTE because ephemeral models are always compiled inline regardless of `--defer`
       -> Correct. Ephemeral models are always compiled as CTEs and injected inline. They never create database objects, so `--defer` does not apply to them.
  [ ] D. dbt skips `fct_reviews` because one of its dependencies is not in the selection
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not skip models because of unselected ephemeral dependencies. Ephemeral models are always compiled inline as CTEs.

Ephemeral models are always inlined as CTEs regardless of `--defer`. - **C) Correct.** Ephemeral models are always compiled as CTEs and injected inline. They never create database objects, so `--defer` does not apply to them. - **D) Incorrect.** dbt does not skip models because of unselected ephemeral dependencies. Ephemeral models are always compiled inline as CTEs. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/defer

Question 63 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO changes would `state:modified` detect by default? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. Changes to a model's SQL body (e.g., modifying the WHERE clause)
       -> Correct. Changes to a model's SQL body are detected by `state:modified` through the `state:modified.body` sub-selector.
  [+] B. Changes to a macro that the model calls
       -> Correct. Changes to macros that a model depends on are detected by `state:modified` through the `state:modified.macros` sub-selector.
  [ ] C. Changes to a model's description in `schema.yml`
       -> Incorrect. Description-only changes in `schema.yml` are not detected by default `state:modified`. You would need `state:modified.persisted_descriptions` for that.
  [ ] D. Changes to the data loaded by an upstream source table
       -> Incorrect. `state:modified` compares project artifacts (code, configs, macros), not warehouse data. If an upstream source table receives new rows but the model's code is unchanged, `state:modified` does not detect it.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Changes to a model's SQL body are detected by `state:modified` through the `state:modified.body` sub-selector. - **B) Correct.** Changes to macros that a model depends on are detected by `state:modified` through the `state:modified.macros` sub-selector. - **C) Incorrect.** Description-only changes in `schema.yml` are not detected by default `state:modified`. You would need `state:modified.persisted_descriptions` for that. - **D) Incorrect.** `state:modified` compares project artifacts (code, configs, macros), not warehouse data. If an upstream source table receives new rows but the model's code is unchanged, `state:modified` does not detect it. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/methods#the-state-method

Question 64 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What does the `+` suffix mean in the selector `state:modified+`?

  [ ] A. It includes only the modified models with enhanced verbose logging
       -> Incorrect. The `+` suffix is a graph operator, not a verbose logging flag.
  [ ] B. It includes the modified models and all of their upstream parents
       -> Incorrect. A `+` prefix (before the selector) means upstream parents. The `+` suffix means downstream.
  [ ] C. It applies a stricter definition of "modified" that includes config changes
       -> Incorrect. The `+` suffix controls graph traversal (downstream inclusion), not the definition of "modified."
  [+] D. It includes the modified models and all of their downstream dependents
       -> Correct. In dbt's graph selection syntax, a `+` suffix means "and all downstream dependents." So `state:modified+` selects changed models and every model downstream of them.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The `+` suffix is a graph operator, not a verbose logging flag. - **B) Incorrect.** A `+` prefix (before the selector) means upstream parents. The `+` suffix means downstream. - **C) Incorrect.** The `+` suffix controls graph traversal (downstream inclusion), not the definition of "modified." - **D) Correct.** In dbt's graph selection syntax, a `+` suffix means "and all downstream dependents." So `state:modified+` selects changed models and every model downstream of them. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/graph-operators

dbt build --select +exposure:executive_dashboard Looking at the lineage graph above, which models are built by this command?

  [ ] A. Only `dim_listings_w_hosts` and `mart_fullmoon_reviews` — the direct parents of the exposure node
       -> Incorrect. The `+` prefix selects all upstream ancestors, not just direct parents. The full lineage chain is included.
  [+] B. Every upstream model: `dim_listings_w_hosts`, `mart_fullmoon_reviews`, and their ancestors
       -> Correct. The `+` prefix in `+exposure:executive_dashboard` traverses the entire upstream DAG. From the graph, this includes both branches: `dim_listings_cleansed` and `dim_hosts_cleansed` into `dim_listings_w_hosts`, and `fct_reviews` into `mart_fullmoon_reviews`.
  [ ] C. Only the `executive_dashboard` exposure node itself, without any upstream models
       -> Incorrect. Without the `+` prefix, `exposure:executive_dashboard` would select only the exposure node itself. The `+` adds all upstream models.
  [ ] D. All models in the project regardless of their connection to the exposure node
       -> Incorrect. The `+` prefix only follows the upstream lineage of the exposure node, not every model in the project.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The `+` prefix selects all upstream ancestors, not just direct parents. The full lineage chain is included. - **B) Correct.** The `+` prefix in `+exposure:executive_dashboard` traverses the entire upstream DAG. From the graph, this includes both branches: `dim_listings_cleansed` and `dim_hosts_cleansed` into `dim_listings_w_hosts`, and `fct_reviews` into `mart_fullmoon_reviews`. - **C) Incorrect.** Without the `+` prefix, `exposure:executive_dashboard` would select only the exposure node itself. The `+` adds all upstream models. - **D) Incorrect.** The `+` prefix only follows the upstream lineage of the exposure node, not every model in the project. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/exposures
