Question 69 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What does the `delete+insert` incremental strategy do differently from `merge` on Snowflake?

  [ ] A. `merge` and `delete+insert` are functionally identical on Snowflake, producing the same SQL operations
       -> Incorrect. `merge` and `delete+insert` use fundamentally different SQL operations on Snowflake (MERGE vs. DELETE then INSERT).
  [ ] B. `delete+insert` truncates the entire target table and reloads all data; `merge` only touches changed rows
       -> Incorrect. `delete+insert` does not truncate the entire table and reload all data; it only deletes rows matching the incoming `unique_key` values, then inserts the incoming rows.
  [+] C. `delete+insert` deletes rows matching the unique key then inserts incoming rows; `merge` updates in place and inserts new ones
       -> Correct. `delete+insert` deletes rows matching the incoming `unique_key`, then inserts all incoming rows. `merge` updates matching rows in place and inserts new ones in a single MERGE statement.
  [ ] D. `merge` requires a `unique_key` to be configured in the model; `delete+insert` works without one
       -> Incorrect. Both strategies benefit from a `unique_key` being configured. Without one, `delete+insert` cannot identify which rows to delete.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `merge` and `delete+insert` use fundamentally different SQL operations on Snowflake (MERGE vs. DELETE then INSERT). - **B) Incorrect.** `delete+insert` does not truncate the entire table and reload all data; it only deletes rows matching the incoming `unique_key` values, then inserts the incoming rows. - **C) Correct.** `delete+insert` deletes rows matching the incoming `unique_key`, then inserts all incoming rows. `merge` updates matching rows in place and inserts new ones in a single MERGE statement. - **D) Incorrect.** Both strategies benefit from a `unique_key` being configured. Without one, `delete+insert` cannot identify which rows to delete. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/incremental-strategy#about-incremental_strategy

Question 70 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO of the following are valid snapshot strategies in dbt? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. `strategy: timestamp` -- uses an `updated_at` column to detect changes
       -> Correct. `timestamp` is a built-in snapshot strategy that uses an `updated_at` column to detect changes in source data.
  [+] B. `strategy: check` -- compares specified columns to detect changes
       -> Correct. `check` is a built-in snapshot strategy that compares specified columns (via `check_cols`) to detect changes.
  [ ] C. `strategy: hash` -- computes a hash of all columns to detect changes
       -> Incorrect. There is no built-in `hash` strategy for snapshots in dbt.
  [ ] D. `strategy: incremental` -- only processes new rows based on a cursor column
       -> Incorrect. There is no built-in `incremental` strategy for snapshots; `incremental` is a model materialization strategy, not a snapshot strategy.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `timestamp` is a built-in snapshot strategy that uses an `updated_at` column to detect changes in source data. - **B) Correct.** `check` is a built-in snapshot strategy that compares specified columns (via `check_cols`) to detect changes. - **C) Incorrect.** There is no built-in `hash` strategy for snapshots in dbt. - **D) Incorrect.** There is no built-in `incremental` strategy for snapshots; `incremental` is a model materialization strategy, not a snapshot strategy. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/snapshots#snapshot-strategies

Question 71 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
You run a model and see this error: Compilation Error in model mart_fullmoon_reviews ( models / mart / mart_fullmoon_reviews . sql ) Could not render : unexpected char '%' at 18 The model contains this line as part of an SQL in a jinja block: COUNT(*) % 7 AS day_of_week_bucket What is causing the error?

  [+] A. The `%` operator is being interpreted as a Jinja delimiter by the template engine
       -> Correct. In Jinja, `%` is part of the block delimiter `{% %}`. The Jinja parser interprets the bare `%` as a block tag, causing a Compilation Error. Use `{{ "%" }}` or `MOD()` instead.
  [ ] B. The `COUNT(*)` function cannot be used with the modulo operator in Snowflake
       -> Incorrect. The `COUNT(*)` function can be used with the modulo operator in Snowflake; the issue is with Jinja parsing, not SQL syntax.
  [ ] C. The `CASE` statement preceding this line has incorrect SQL syntax
       -> Incorrect. The error message references the `%` character specifically, not a preceding CASE statement.
  [ ] D. The model is missing a required `GROUP BY` clause
       -> Incorrect. A missing GROUP BY would produce a Database Error at execution time, not a Compilation Error about an unexpected character.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** In Jinja, `%` is part of the block delimiter `{% %}`. The Jinja parser interprets the bare `%` as a block tag, causing a Compilation Error. Use `{{ "%" }}` or `MOD()` instead. - **B) Incorrect.** The `COUNT(*)` function can be used with the modulo operator in Snowflake; the issue is with Jinja parsing, not SQL syntax. - **C) Incorrect.** The error message references the `%` character specifically, not a preceding CASE statement. - **D) Incorrect.** A missing GROUP BY would produce a Database Error at execution time, not a Compilation Error about an unexpected character. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/jinja-macros#jinja

Question 72 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):

A developer creates a second model with the same name `src_listings` in a different subfolder and gets this error: Compilation Error dbt found two models with the name "src_listings" . What must you do to resolve this?

  [ ] A. Add a `schema` config to each model to differentiate them
       -> Incorrect. Adding a `schema` config changes the target schema in the warehouse but does not resolve the duplicate model name issue within the dbt project.
  [ ] B. Add an `alias` config to both models to create different table names
       -> Incorrect. `alias` changes the table name in the warehouse but does not change the model name used in `ref()`, so the duplicate name error persists.
  [ ] C. Place the models in different directories and use `ref('directory.src_listings')`
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not support `ref('directory.model_name')` syntax; `ref()` uses model names, not file paths.
  [+] D. Rename one of the models so all model names are unique across the entire project
       -> Correct. All model names must be unique across the entire project regardless of directory. Renaming one of the models is the correct fix.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Adding a `schema` config changes the target schema in the warehouse but does not resolve the duplicate model name issue within the dbt project. - **B) Incorrect.** `alias` changes the table name in the warehouse but does not change the model name used in `ref()`, so the duplicate name error persists. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt does not support `ref('directory.model_name')` syntax; `ref()` uses model names, not file paths. - **D) Correct.** All model names must be unique across the entire project regardless of directory. Renaming one of the models is the correct fix. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/faqs/Models/unique-model-names

The four meta columns are `dbt_scd_id`, `dbt_valid_from`, `dbt_valid_to`, and `dbt_updated_at`. - **C) Incorrect.** `dbt_scd_id` is a real snapshot meta column used as a surrogate key for each record version. - **D) Incorrect.** `dbt_updated_at` is a real snapshot meta column that stores the value of the tracked timestamp. Type: SINGLE
Which of the following is a limitation of dbt Python models?

  [ ] A. They cannot reference other dbt models using `dbt.ref()`
       -> Incorrect. Python models can reference other dbt models using `dbt.ref()`.
  [ ] B. They cannot be used as incremental models
       -> Incorrect. Python models can be used as incremental models.
  [ ] C. They cannot be referenced by downstream SQL models using `ref()`
       -> Incorrect. Python models fully participate in the DAG and can be referenced by downstream SQL models using `ref()`.
  [+] D. They can only be materialized as tables, not views
       -> Correct. Python models can only be materialized as `table` or `incremental` because the Python code must execute and write results to the warehouse. Views are not supported.

Views are not supported. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/python-models#materializations

Question 75 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO statements about the `grants` config in dbt are TRUE? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. `grants` can be set in `dbt_project.yml`, in a model's `config()` block, or in the model's YAML properties
       -> Correct. Like other configs, `grants` can be set in `dbt_project.yml`, in a model's `config()` block, or in its YAML properties, with the most specific level taking precedence.
  [+] B. dbt applies `grants` as part of the model's materialization, after the table or view is created
       -> Correct. dbt applies grants at the end of a model's materialization, once the relation exists, so the privileges match the config on every run.
  [ ] C. `grants` only works on dbt Cloud and is ignored by dbt Core
       -> Incorrect. `grants` is a dbt Core config supported on adapters that implement it -- it is not limited to dbt Cloud.
  [ ] D. `grants` are applied before the model's SQL runs, as an automatic pre-hook
       -> Incorrect. Grants are applied after the relation is built, not as a pre-hook before the model's SQL runs.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Like other configs, `grants` can be set in `dbt_project.yml`, in a model's `config()` block, or in its YAML properties, with the most specific level taking precedence. - **B) Correct.** dbt applies grants at the end of a model's materialization, once the relation exists, so the privileges match the config on every run. - **C) Incorrect.** `grants` is a dbt Core config supported on adapters that implement it -- it is not limited to dbt Cloud. - **D) Incorrect.** Grants are applied after the relation is built, not as a pre-hook before the model's SQL runs. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-configs/grants

  [ ] D. `hard_deletes: invalidate` -- to handle deleted records in the source table
       -> Incorrect. `hard_deletes: invalidate` is an optional configuration for handling deleted records in the source table, not a requirement of the `check` strategy.

You can list specific columns or use `check_cols='all'`. - **D) Incorrect.** `hard_deletes: invalidate` is an optional configuration for handling deleted records in the source table, not a requirement of the `check` strategy. Type: SINGLE
According to dbt best practices, what is the recommended naming convention for staging models?

  [ ] A. `staging_<source>_<entity>`
       -> Incorrect. `staging_` is not the recommended prefix -- the convention uses the shorter `stg_` prefix.
  [+] B. `stg_<source>__<entity>`
       -> Correct. The dbt community convention uses `stg_` followed by the source name, a double underscore `__`, and the entity name (e.g., `stg_airbnb__listings`).
  [ ] C. `raw_<source>_<entity>`
       -> Incorrect. The `raw_` prefix is not the convention for staging models -- staging models transform raw data.
  [ ] D. `src_<entity>`
       -> Incorrect. `src_` is not the standard prefix, and this format omits the source name and double underscore delimiter.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `staging_` is not the recommended prefix -- the convention uses the shorter `stg_` prefix. - **B) Correct.** The dbt community convention uses `stg_` followed by the source name, a double underscore `__`, and the entity name (e.g., `stg_airbnb__listings`). - **C) Incorrect.** The `raw_` prefix is not the convention for staging models -- staging models transform raw data. - **D) Incorrect.** `src_` is not the standard prefix, and this format omits the source name and double underscore delimiter. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/best-practices/how-we-structure/2-staging

Question 78 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
In which TWO scenarios is `dbt run --full-refresh` necessary for an incremental model? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. You changed the columns in the `generate_surrogate_key` call (affecting the primary key)
       -> Correct. Changing surrogate key columns means historical data has inconsistent keys that need to be regenerated from scratch.
  [ ] B. You changed the description of the model in `schema.yml` without modifying any SQL logic
       -> Incorrect. Description changes in `schema.yml` without modifying SQL logic have no effect on model data and never require a full refresh.
  [+] C. You changed the incremental filter from `review_date >` to `review_date >=` inside the `{% if is_incremental() %}` block
       -> Correct. Changing the incremental filter logic means previous runs may have missed or double-counted data, requiring a full reload to ensure consistency.
  [ ] D. You added a new data test to the model in `schema.yml` without changing the model SQL
       -> Incorrect. Adding a new data test to `schema.yml` without changing the model SQL does not affect model data and never requires a full refresh.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Changing surrogate key columns means historical data has inconsistent keys that need to be regenerated from scratch. - **B) Incorrect.** Description changes in `schema.yml` without modifying SQL logic have no effect on model data and never require a full refresh. - **C) Correct.** Changing the incremental filter logic means previous runs may have missed or double-counted data, requiring a full reload to ensure consistency. - **D) Incorrect.** Adding a new data test to `schema.yml` without changing the model SQL does not affect model data and never requires a full refresh. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/incremental-models#how-do-i-rebuild-an-incremental-model

Question 79 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO statements about `on-run-start` and `on-run-end` hooks are correct? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. `on-run-start` hooks execute before ANY model in the run begins
       -> Correct. `on-run-start` hooks run once at the very beginning of a dbt invocation, before any model execution begins.
  [ ] B. `on-run-start` hooks execute once per model, before each model starts
       -> Incorrect. `on-run-start` hooks are not per-model hooks. Per-model hooks are `pre-hook` and `post-hook`.
  [+] C. `on-run-end` hooks can access the `results` variable containing the run results
       -> Correct. `on-run-end` hooks run once after all models finish, regardless of success or failure, and have access to the `results` variable containing run results.
  [ ] D. `on-run-end` hooks only run if ALL models in the run succeed
       -> Incorrect. `on-run-end` hooks run regardless of whether all models succeeded or some failed. They always execute after the run completes.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `on-run-start` hooks run once at the very beginning of a dbt invocation, before any model execution begins. - **B) Incorrect.** `on-run-start` hooks are not per-model hooks. Per-model hooks are `pre-hook` and `post-hook`. - **C) Correct.** `on-run-end` hooks run once after all models finish, regardless of success or failure, and have access to the `results` variable containing run results. - **D) Incorrect.** `on-run-end` hooks run regardless of whether all models succeeded or some failed. They always execute after the run completes. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/project-configs/on-run-start-on-run-end

Question 81 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
You need to run seeds, models, snapshots, and tests -- all respecting the dependency graph -- in a single command. Which command accomplishes this?

  [ ] A. `dbt run --full` (builds all resource types at once)
       -> Incorrect. `dbt run --full` is not a valid dbt command; there is no `--full` flag on `dbt run`.
  [+] B. `dbt build` (runs all resource types in DAG order)
       -> Correct. `dbt build` runs seeds, models, snapshots, and tests in DAG order, interleaving tests with their upstream models.
  [ ] C. `dbt run && dbt test` (chained in two passes)
       -> Incorrect. `dbt run && dbt test` chained in two passes runs all models first then all tests separately, losing the interleaving benefit and not including seeds or snapshots.
  [ ] D. `dbt execute --all` (processes every node type)
       -> Incorrect. `dbt execute --all` is not a valid dbt command; `execute` is not a dbt CLI verb.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `dbt run --full` is not a valid dbt command; there is no `--full` flag on `dbt run`. - **B) Correct.** `dbt build` runs seeds, models, snapshots, and tests in DAG order, interleaving tests with their upstream models. - **C) Incorrect.** `dbt run && dbt test` chained in two passes runs all models first then all tests separately, losing the interleaving benefit and not including seeds or snapshots. - **D) Incorrect.** `dbt execute --all` is not a valid dbt command; `execute` is not a dbt CLI verb. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/commands/build

Question 83 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Which of the following best describes a macro in dbt?

  [ ] A. A pre-built model template that ships with dbt Core and runs automatically during `dbt run`
       -> Incorrect. Macros are not pre-built model templates -- they are reusable Jinja code blocks that generate SQL.
  [+] B. A reusable Jinja code block defined in the `macros/` directory, callable from models, tests, or other macros
       -> Correct. Macros are reusable Jinja code blocks defined in `.sql` files in the `macros/` directory. They accept arguments and are called with `{{ macro_name(args) }}` syntax from models, tests, or other macros.
  [ ] C. A Python script stored in the project root that automates dbt CLI commands at build time
       -> Incorrect. Macros are Jinja templates, not Python scripts. They do not automate CLI commands at build time.
  [ ] D. A database stored procedure that dbt creates and registers in the warehouse at runtime
       -> Incorrect. Macros generate SQL at compile time -- they do not create or register stored procedures in the warehouse.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Macros are not pre-built model templates -- they are reusable Jinja code blocks that generate SQL. - **B) Correct.** Macros are reusable Jinja code blocks defined in `.sql` files in the `macros/` directory. They accept arguments and are called with `{{ macro_name(args) }}` syntax from models, tests, or other macros. - **C) Incorrect.** Macros are Jinja templates, not Python scripts. They do not automate CLI commands at build time. - **D) Incorrect.** Macros generate SQL at compile time -- they do not create or register stored procedures in the warehouse. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/jinja-macros#macros

  [ ] C. dbt logs a deprecation warning about the missing column but completes the build
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not issue warnings and continue for contract violations. The build fails immediately.

       -> Incorrect. dbt never automatically modifies a contract. Contracts are the source of truth and must be manually updated.

Any deviation — whether a missing column or a type mismatch — causes a build failure. - **B) Correct.** With `contract: {enforced: true}`, all columns declared in the YAML must be present in the model output. The build fails immediately. - **D) Incorrect.** dbt never automatically modifies a contract. Contracts are the source of truth and must be manually updated. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-contracts

If the SQL returns `listing_id` as VARCHAR instead of INTEGER, the database rejects the type mismatch. - **D) Incorrect.** The contract is enforced during `dbt run` (when the model is built), not only during `dbt test`. Question 86 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A model `dim_listings_cleansed` defines versions `v: 1` and `v: 2`, with `latest_version: 2`. A downstream model needs to pin to version 1 specifically. How is that reference written?

  [+] A. `ref('dim_listings_cleansed', v=1)`
       -> Correct. A specific version is pinned with the `v` keyword argument: `ref('dim_listings_cleansed', v=1)`. Omitting `v` resolves the ref to `latest_version` (here, v2).
  [ ] B. `ref('dim_listings_cleansed', version=1)`
       -> Incorrect. The keyword argument is `v`, not `version` -- `ref('model', version=1)` is not valid syntax.
  [ ] C. `ref('dim_listings_cleansed_v1')`
       -> Incorrect. Versions are not separate models with a `_v1` suffix; they share one model name and are selected through the `v` argument.
  [ ] D. `ref('dim_listings_cleansed', 1)`
       -> Incorrect. A bare positional `1` is not a version argument -- the second positional argument of `ref()` is a package name, so the version must be passed as `v=1`.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** A specific version is pinned with the `v` keyword argument: `ref('dim_listings_cleansed', v=1)`. Omitting `v` resolves the ref to `latest_version` (here, v2). - **B) Incorrect.** The keyword argument is `v`, not `version` -- `ref('model', version=1)` is not valid syntax. - **C) Incorrect.** Versions are not separate models with a `_v1` suffix; they share one model name and are selected through the `v` argument. - **D) Incorrect.** A bare positional `1` is not a version argument -- the second positional argument of `ref()` is a package name, so the version must be passed as `v=1`. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-versions

Type: SINGLE
Before opening a PR, a developer runs dbt build --select +staging --empty and the entire build (models, tests, the lot) succeeds in 30 seconds. The PR is merged. The first scheduled production run after merge fails: a `not_null` test on `stg_orders.order_id` errors with "Got 4 results, expected 0."   [ ] A. The `--empty` flag skips data tests entirely; the `not_null` test was never evaluated in the dry-run, so the failure only appeared in the post-merge run

  [ ] B. The `--empty` flag short-circuits model SQL and only validates YAML configuration, so source-data nulls are invisible to it; the test would never catch this class of bug
       -> Incorrect. `--empty` does run the model SQL; it just constrains the result to zero rows. YAML validation alone wouldn't trigger a `not_null` evaluation either way.

       -> Correct. `--empty` performs a dry-run by limiting models to zero rows (effectively a `where false`). The model SQL still compiles and executes, but data tests like `not_null` and `unique` evaluate against an empty table and pass vacuously. Test failures driven by actual source data only appear in a normal run.
  [ ] D. The `--empty` flag uses a representative sample of source rows; the sample happened to omit the rows containing nulls, which is a known sampling-error class for null detection
       -> Incorrect. Sampling is what `--sample` does. `--empty` is not statistical — it is deterministic zero-row materialization.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `--empty` does not skip tests. Tests are evaluated normally — but against an empty (0-row) build of the model. - **B) Incorrect.** `--empty` does run the model SQL; it just constrains the result to zero rows. YAML validation alone wouldn't trigger a `not_null` evaluation either way. - **C) Correct.** `--empty` performs a dry-run by limiting models to zero rows (effectively a `where false`). The model SQL still compiles and executes, but data tests like `not_null` and `unique` evaluate against an empty table and pass vacuously. Test failures driven by actual source data only appear in a normal run. - **D) Incorrect.** Sampling is what `--sample` does. `--empty` is not statistical — it is deterministic zero-row materialization. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/commands/build#the---empty-flag

  [+] A. A model references `{{ ref('src_review') }}` but the correct model name is `src_reviews`
       -> Correct. A misspelled `ref()` fails during DAG resolution because dbt cannot find the referenced model, producing a Compilation Error.
  [+] B. A model has a `{% for %}` loop that is missing its `{% endfor %}` tag
       -> Correct. A missing `{% endfor %}` is a Jinja syntax error caught during the parsing phase, producing a Compilation Error.
  [ ] C. A model has a missing comma between two column expressions in the SELECT statement
       -> Incorrect. A missing comma produces valid Jinja but invalid SQL, so it passes compilation and fails as a Database Error at execution time.
  [+] D. A Jinja variable `{{ var('filter_date') }}` is used but never defined in `dbt_project.yml` and no default is provided
       -> Correct. An undefined `var()` with no default cannot be resolved during Jinja rendering, producing a Compilation Error.
  [ ] E. A model's LEFT JOIN references a column that does not exist in the joined table
       -> Incorrect. A non-existent column produces valid Jinja but invalid SQL, so it passes compilation and fails as a Database Error at execution time.

What type of error does a circular reference between two models produce?

  [ ] A. Database Error
       -> Incorrect. A Database Error occurs when SQL reaches the warehouse and fails. Circular references are caught before any SQL is sent.

       -> Correct. Circular dependencies are detected during the parsing/compilation phase when dbt builds the DAG. Since it cannot determine execution order, it raises a Compilation Error.

       -> Incorrect. Runtime Errors are a general category; the specific error type for circular dependencies is a Compilation Error.
  [ ] D. Dependency Error
       -> Incorrect. "Dependency Error" is not a recognized error type in dbt's error classification.

Since it cannot determine execution order, it raises a Compilation Error. - **C) Incorrect.** Runtime Errors are a general category; the specific error type for circular dependencies is a Compilation Error. - **D) Incorrect.** "Dependency Error" is not a recognized error type in dbt's error classification. Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO of the following scenarios produce a Database Error (not a Compilation Error)? (Choose 2)

  [ ] A. A Jinja `{% if %}` block in a model references an undefined macro in its condition
       -> Incorrect. Referencing an undefined macro is caught during Jinja rendering at compile time — before any SQL reaches the warehouse — making it a Compilation Error.

       -> Correct. When the warehouse tries to resolve the view's dependency at query time, it discovers the base table is missing and raises a Database Error. The model compiled successfully but fails during execution.

Explanation:

The error only occurs when the warehouse engine attempts to execute the function call and cannot resolve it, making this a Database Error. - **C) Incorrect.** A tab character in YAML produces a parsing error during `dbt parse`, before any model is compiled or run. This is a Compilation Error. - **D) Correct.** When the warehouse tries to resolve the view's dependency at query time, it discovers the base table is missing and raises a Database Error. The model compiled successfully but fails during execution. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/guides/debug-errors#types-of-errors

Both thresholds are evaluated independently, with `error_if` controlling error status and `warn_if` controlling warnings. - **D) Incorrect.** NULL values are precisely what the `not_null` test checks for. Question 96 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What is the difference between the `target/compiled/` and `target/run/` directories?

  [ ] A. `compiled/` contains unresolved Jinja templates and `run/` contains the fully resolved SQL output
       -> Incorrect. `compiled/` contains fully resolved Jinja (not unresolved), and `run/` contains the DDL-wrapped version of the same SQL.
  [ ] B. They contain identical SQL files with the same content; `run/` is simply a backup copy of `compiled/`
       -> Incorrect. The two directories serve different purposes -- `run/` is not a backup of `compiled/`.
  [ ] C. `compiled/` is generated only for development builds and `run/` only for production builds
       -> Incorrect. Both directories are generated during every build regardless of environment -- they are not split by dev/prod.
  [+] D. `compiled/` contains the pure SELECT with Jinja resolved; `run/` contains the full DDL-wrapped SQL sent to the database
       -> Correct. `target/compiled/` contains the pure SELECT with all Jinja resolved. `target/run/` contains the full SQL sent to the database, including DDL/DML wrappers such as `CREATE TABLE AS` or `CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW`.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `compiled/` contains fully resolved Jinja (not unresolved), and `run/` contains the DDL-wrapped version of the same SQL. - **B) Incorrect.** The two directories serve different purposes -- `run/` is not a backup of `compiled/`. - **C) Incorrect.** Both directories are generated during every build regardless of environment -- they are not split by dev/prod. - **D) Correct.** `target/compiled/` contains the pure SELECT with all Jinja resolved. `target/run/` contains the full SQL sent to the database, including DDL/DML wrappers such as `CREATE TABLE AS` or `CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW`. Question 97 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Running `dbt compile` on `dim_listings_cleansed` produces this error: Compilation Error in model dim_listings_cleansed ( models / dim_listings_cleansed . sql ) unexpected end of template , expected 'endfor' . What is the most likely cause?

  [+] A. A `{% for %}` loop in the model's Jinja template is missing its closing `{% endfor %}` tag
       -> Correct. The error "unexpected end of template, expected 'endfor'" means Jinja2 reached the end of the file while still inside an open `{% for %}` loop. Adding the missing `{% endfor %}` tag resolves this.
  [ ] B. The model references an upstream model that has not been built yet
       -> Incorrect. Missing upstream models produce a `Relation not found` or `TargetNotFound` error, not a Jinja template rendering error.
  [ ] C. A tab character was used instead of spaces for indentation inside the Jinja block
       -> Incorrect. Tab indentation causes a YAML parsing error in `schema.yml`, not a Jinja template compilation error in model SQL.
  [ ] D. The model's SQL contains a subquery that dbt does not support
       -> Incorrect. dbt supports subqueries in models. This error is specific to unclosed Jinja template blocks, not SQL structure.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** The error "unexpected end of template, expected 'endfor'" means Jinja2 reached the end of the file while still inside an open `{% for %}` loop. Adding the missing `{% endfor %}` tag resolves this. - **B) Incorrect.** Missing upstream models produce a `Relation not found` or `TargetNotFound` error, not a Jinja template rendering error. - **C) Incorrect.** Tab indentation causes a YAML parsing error in `schema.yml`, not a Jinja template compilation error in model SQL. - **D) Incorrect.** dbt supports subqueries in models. This error is specific to unclosed Jinja template blocks, not SQL structure. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/guides/debug-errors#jinja-errors

Question 98 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Trace through this Jinja macro: {% macro build_listing_filter ( room_types ) %} {% set where_clause = '' %} {% for rt in room_types %} {% if loop . first %} {% set where_clause = "WHERE room_type = '" ~ rt ~ "'" %} {% else %} {% set where_clause = where_clause ~ " OR room_type = '" ~ rt ~ "'" %} {% endif %} {% endfor %} {{ where_clause }} {% endmacro %} Called with: ` {{ build_listing_filter(['Entire home/apt', 'Private room']) }} ` What does this macro output?

  [ ] A. The full clause: `WHERE room_type = 'Entire home/apt' OR room_type = 'Private room'`
       -> Incorrect. Due to Jinja scoping, the `{% set %}` inside the `{% for %}` loop creates a local variable that does not update the outer `where_clause`. The full clause is never produced.
  [ ] B. Only the second iteration's output: `OR room_type = 'Private room'`
       -> Incorrect. The outer `where_clause` is not updated by any loop iteration. Only the second iteration's output appears in the loop's local scope, not outside it.
  [+] C. An empty string, because Jinja scoping prevents the outer variable from updating inside the loop
       -> Correct. This is a classic Jinja scoping gotcha. `{% set %}` inside a `{% for %}` loop creates a variable in the loop's local scope, not the outer scope. After the loop ends, `where_clause` reverts to the empty string.
  [ ] D. Only the first iteration's output: `WHERE room_type = 'Entire home/apt'`
       -> Incorrect. Only the first iteration's value would be set locally, but the outer `where_clause` is not affected. The output is an empty string, not just the first clause.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Due to Jinja scoping, the `{% set %}` inside the `{% for %}` loop creates a local variable that does not update the outer `where_clause`. The full clause is never produced. - **B) Incorrect.** The outer `where_clause` is not updated by any loop iteration. Only the second iteration's output appears in the loop's local scope, not outside it. - **C) Correct.** This is a classic Jinja scoping gotcha. `{% set %}` inside a `{% for %}` loop creates a variable in the loop's local scope, not the outer scope. After the loop ends, `where_clause` reverts to the empty string. - **D) Incorrect.** Only the first iteration's value would be set locally, but the outer `where_clause` is not affected. The output is an empty string, not just the first clause. Reference: https://jinja.palletsprojects.com/en/3.1.x/templates/#assignments

Type: SINGLE
Many dimension models in your DAG are independent and could run in parallel. Which approach is MOST likely to reduce total run time?

  [+] A. Increasing the `--threads` value to allow more models to build concurrently
       -> Correct. Increasing `--threads` allows dbt to build more independent models concurrently, directly reducing total run time when models are independent in the DAG.
  [ ] B. Changing all models to `materialized='view'` to avoid table creation overhead
       -> Incorrect. While views avoid table creation overhead, they do not improve parallelism and may cause performance issues at query time for downstream consumers.
  [ ] C. Adding `+tags: ['parallel']` to models and running tagged models in separate commands
       -> Incorrect. Running tagged models in separate commands adds orchestration complexity and does not improve parallelism compared to simply increasing threads.
  [ ] D. Splitting the project into multiple dbt projects and running them sequentially
       -> Incorrect. Splitting into multiple projects and running them sequentially would increase complexity without improving parallelism.

Explanation:

Question 101 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Which statement about `dbt clone` is TRUE?

  [ ] A. `dbt clone` creates a full physical copy of the data in the target schema
       -> Incorrect. `dbt clone` creates zero-copy clones, not full physical copies. The cloned table references the same underlying storage.
  [ ] B. `dbt clone` creates a new dbt project from a template
       -> Incorrect. `dbt clone` operates on database objects in the warehouse, not on dbt project templates.
  [ ] C. `dbt clone` requires the `--full-refresh` flag to work
       -> Incorrect. `dbt clone` does not require `--full-refresh`; it works directly without this flag.
  [+] D. `dbt clone` uses zero-copy cloning for tables where the warehouse supports it, and creates a pointer view for views
       -> Correct. On warehouses that support it (Snowflake, BigQuery, Databricks), `dbt clone` creates a zero-copy clone of a table. For views -- or any object that cannot be zero-copy cloned -- dbt instead builds a pointer view (`select * from` the source), so views are not skipped.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `dbt clone` creates zero-copy clones, not full physical copies. The cloned table references the same underlying storage. - **B) Incorrect.** `dbt clone` operates on database objects in the warehouse, not on dbt project templates. - **C) Incorrect.** `dbt clone` does not require `--full-refresh`; it works directly without this flag. - **D) Correct.** On warehouses that support it (Snowflake, BigQuery, Databricks), `dbt clone` creates a zero-copy clone of a table. For views -- or any object that cannot be zero-copy cloned -- dbt instead builds a pointer view (`select * from` the source), so views are not skipped. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/commands/clone

Type: SINGLE
Which cron expression schedules a job to run every weekday (Monday through Friday) at 6:00 AM UTC?

  [ ] A. `0 6 * * *`
       -> Incorrect. `0 6 * * *` runs every day at 6 AM, including weekends. The fifth field `*` matches all days of the week.
  [ ] B. `6 0 * * 1-5`
       -> Incorrect. `6 0 * * 1-5` has the hour and minute reversed — this runs at 12:06 AM, not 6:00 AM.
  [+] C. `0 6 * * 1-5`
       -> Correct. `0 6 * * 1-5` means minute 0, hour 6, any day of month, any month, Monday through Friday (weekdays only).
  [ ] D. `0 6 1-5 * *`
       -> Incorrect. `0 6 1-5 * *` incorrectly places the weekday restriction in the day-of-month field, meaning it runs on the 1st through 5th of each month instead of Monday through Friday.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `0 6 * * *` runs every day at 6 AM, including weekends. The fifth field `*` matches all days of the week. - **B) Incorrect.** `6 0 * * 1-5` has the hour and minute reversed — this runs at 12:06 AM, not 6:00 AM. - **C) Correct.** `0 6 * * 1-5` means minute 0, hour 6, any day of month, any month, Monday through Friday (weekdays only). - **D) Incorrect.** `0 6 1-5 * *` incorrectly places the weekday restriction in the day-of-month field, meaning it runs on the 1st through 5th of each month instead of Monday through Friday.        -> Incorrect. Unit tests still execute SQL against the warehouse using mock data; they do not skip warehouse execution entirely.
  [+] B. Unit tests validate transformation logic using mock input rows without depending on production data
       -> Correct. dbt unit tests let you define `given` (mock inputs) and `expect` (expected outputs) rows. The model SQL runs against the mock inputs in isolation, allowing you to validate transformation logic without depending on production data state.
  [ ] C. Unit tests can check whether source tables contain duplicate records
       -> Incorrect. Duplicate checks on source data are a job for data tests (`unique`). Unit tests are for validating model transformation logic, not source data quality.
  [ ] D. Unit tests automatically generate test data from the model's schema definition
       -> Incorrect. Unit tests require manually specified `given` rows in YAML. dbt does not auto-generate test data from schema definitions.

OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Unit tests still execute SQL against the warehouse using mock data; they do not skip warehouse execution entirely. - **B) Correct.** dbt unit tests let you define `given` (mock inputs) and `expect` (expected outputs) rows. The model SQL runs against the mock inputs in isolation, allowing you to validate transformation logic without depending on production data state. - **C) Incorrect.** Duplicate checks on source data are a job for data tests (`unique`). Unit tests are for validating model transformation logic, not source data quality. - **D) Incorrect.** Unit tests require manually specified `given` rows in YAML. dbt does not auto-generate test data from schema definitions.        -> Incorrect. Generic tests in `schema.yml` can test at both column and model levels, not just single columns.
  [ ] D. There is no functional difference -- they are two syntaxes for the same thing
       -> Incorrect. They are functionally different. Generic tests use parameterized macros while singular tests are standalone SQL files.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Tests in `schema.yml` are generic tests applied declaratively to models and columns. Tests in `tests/` are singular tests with custom SQL returning zero rows on success. - **B) Incorrect.** Both types of tests are compiled similarly. There is no pre-compilation advantage for schema-defined tests. - **C) Incorrect.** Generic tests in `schema.yml` can test at both column and model levels, not just single columns. - **D) Incorrect.** They are functionally different.        -> Incorrect. There is no `filter` config for dbt tests; this is not a valid test configuration property.
  [ ] B. `rows: "last_7_days"` as a built-in test time window selector
       -> Incorrect. There is no `rows` config or built-in time window selector for dbt tests.
  [ ] C. `limit: 7` to restrict the test to only 7 rows of the result set
       -> Incorrect. The `limit` config restricts the number of failing rows returned in results, not which rows are tested.
  [+] D. `where: "review_date >= current_date - interval '7 days'"` in the test config
       -> Correct. The `where` config adds a WHERE clause to the test query, limiting which rows are evaluated during the test.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** There is no `filter` config for dbt tests; this is not a valid test configuration property. - **B) Incorrect.** There is no `rows` config or built-in time window selector for dbt tests. - **C) Incorrect.** The `limit` config restricts the number of failing rows returned in results, not which rows are tested. - **D) Correct.** The `where` config adds a WHERE clause to the test query, limiting which rows are evaluated during the test. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-configs/where

       -> Incorrect. The `{{ doc() }}` call references an existing doc block wherever it is used; it does not create one inline.

The `{{ doc("...") }}` function in YAML references them. - **D) Incorrect.** The `{{ doc() }}` call references an existing doc block wherever it is used; it does not create one inline.        -> Correct. Source column descriptions require the `columns:` key nested under the source table definition, following the `sources: > tables: > columns:` hierarchy.

       -> Incorrect. Model descriptions can be defined inline with `description:` in YAML or via `{{ doc() }}` blocks. They are not limited to `.md` doc blocks.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Source descriptions are defined under the `sources:` key in YAML, while model descriptions are defined under the `models:` key. - **B) Incorrect.** Sources and models have different YAML structures. Source documentation nests under `sources: > tables: > columns:`, while models use `models: > columns:`. - **C) Correct.** Source column descriptions require the `columns:` key nested under the source table definition, following the `sources: > tables: > columns:` hierarchy. - **D) Incorrect.** Model descriptions can be defined inline with `description:` in YAML or via `{{ doc() }}` blocks. They are not limited to `.md` doc blocks. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/documentation

       -> Correct. The `loaded_at_field` must be a timestamp or datetime column so dbt can compare its max value against the current time to determine freshness.

  [+] A. `result:error`
       -> Correct. `result:error` is a valid selector that targets nodes with runtime or database errors from the previous run.
  [ ] B. `result:success`
       -> Incorrect. While `result:success` is valid for selecting models that succeeded, it selects nodes that already passed — not the ones you need to re-run.
  [+] C. `result:skipped`
       -> Correct. `result:skipped` is a valid selector that targets nodes that were skipped, often because an upstream dependency failed.
  [ ] D. `result:incomplete`
       -> Incorrect. There is no `result:incomplete` status in dbt. The valid result statuses are `error`, `success`, `fail`, `warn`, `pass`, and `skipped`.

Explanation:

The valid result statuses are `error`, `success`, `fail`, `warn`, `pass`, and `skipped`. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/methods#the-result-method

Question 121 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What does the `--defer` flag do in a Slim CI pipeline?

  [ ] A. It defers the execution of failed models to a later retry step in the pipeline
       -> Incorrect. `--defer` does not defer failed models for a later retry step; that is what `dbt retry` does.
  [ ] B. It schedules the current run to execute only after all production jobs complete
       -> Incorrect. `--defer` does not schedule runs to wait for production jobs; it resolves references at execution time.
  [ ] C. It skips building models that have not changed compared to the previous state
       -> Incorrect. Skipping unchanged models is handled by `state:modified` selection, not by `--defer`.
  [+] D. It tells dbt to use production database objects for any `ref()` not being built in the current run
       -> Correct. `--defer` tells dbt to resolve `ref()` calls for models not in the current run to the corresponding production objects, avoiding the need to build the entire DAG in CI.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `--defer` does not defer failed models for a later retry step; that is what `dbt retry` does. - **B) Incorrect.** `--defer` does not schedule runs to wait for production jobs; it resolves references at execution time. - **C) Incorrect.** Skipping unchanged models is handled by `state:modified` selection, not by `--defer`. - **D) Correct.** `--defer` tells dbt to resolve `ref()` calls for models not in the current run to the corresponding production objects, avoiding the need to build the entire DAG in CI. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/defer

A CI/CD pipeline uses this command: dbt build -- select state : modified + result : error + -- defer -- state ./ prod - artifacts -- target ci What does the space between `state:modified+` and `result:error+` mean for selection?

  [+] A. It takes the UNION of modified models (plus downstream) and previously errored models (plus downstream) -- both sets are included
       -> Correct. A space between `--select` arguments means UNION (OR). Both `state:modified+` and `result:error+` are evaluated, and nodes matching either criterion are selected.
  [ ] B. It further filters to only include modified models that previously errored, plus their downstream dependents
       -> Incorrect. A space means UNION (OR), not further filtering. To get an intersection (AND), you would use a comma separator.
  [ ] C. It takes the INTERSECTION: only models that are both modified AND previously errored, plus their downstream
       -> Incorrect. A space means UNION (OR), not INTERSECTION (AND). The comma operator would create an intersection.
  [ ] D. It overrides `state:modified+` and only runs previously errored models
       -> Incorrect. The second selector does not override the first. Both selectors are combined using UNION logic.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** A space between `--select` arguments means UNION (OR). Both `state:modified+` and `result:error+` are evaluated, and nodes matching either criterion are selected. - **B) Incorrect.** A space means UNION (OR), not further filtering. To get an intersection (AND), you would use a comma separator. - **C) Incorrect.** A space means UNION (OR), not INTERSECTION (AND). The comma operator would create an intersection. - **D) Incorrect.** The second selector does not override the first. Both selectors are combined using UNION logic. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/set-operators

Question 130 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_2.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Looking at the lineage graph above, which TWO statements are correct?

  [+] A. `dbt ls --select @mart_fullmoon_reviews lists every node in the graph
       -> Correct. The DAG has only one component and therefore to the iterative logic of @ will select all.
  [+] B. `dbt ls --select dim_listings_cleansed+` lists `dim_listings_cleansed`, `dim_listings_w_hosts`, and the `executive_dashboard` exposure
       -> Correct. The `+` suffix in `dim_listings_cleansed+` selects all downstream dependents. From the graph, `dim_listings_cleansed` flows into `dim_listings_w_hosts`, which flows into the `executive_dashboard` exposure.
  [ ] C. `dbt ls --select dim_hosts_cleansed+` lists `dim_hosts_cleansed` and `fct_reviews`
       -> Incorrect. `dim_hosts_cleansed+` selects downstream dependents of `dim_hosts_cleansed`. From the graph, that is `dim_listings_w_hosts` and `executive_dashboard` — not `fct_reviews`, which is on a separate branch.
  [ ] D. `dbt ls --select fct_reviews+` lists `fct_reviews`, `mart_fullmoon_reviews`, and `dim_listings_w_hosts`
       -> Incorrect. `fct_reviews+` selects `fct_reviews`, `mart_fullmoon_reviews`, and `executive_dashboard`. `dim_listings_w_hosts` is not downstream of `fct_reviews` — it is on a separate branch.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct. The DAG has only one component and due to the iterative logic of @ they will all be selected - **B) Correct.** The `+` suffix in `dim_listings_cleansed+` selects all downstream dependents. From the graph, `dim_listings_cleansed` flows into `dim_listings_w_hosts`, which flows into the `executive_dashboard` exposure. - **C) Incorrect.** `dim_hosts_cleansed+` selects downstream dependents of `dim_hosts_cleansed`. From the graph, that is `dim_listings_w_hosts` and `executive_dashboard` — not `fct_reviews`, which is on a separate branch. - **D) Incorrect.** `fct_reviews+` selects `fct_reviews`, `mart_fullmoon_reviews`, and `executive_dashboard`. `dim_listings_w_hosts` is not downstream of `fct_reviews` — it is on a separate branch. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/graph-operators

  [ ] A. An auto-incrementing integer starting from 1 for each row in the result set
       -> Incorrect. `generate_surrogate_key()` does not produce auto-incrementing integers -- it produces hash values.
  [+] B. A deterministic hash value based on the combination of the specified columns
       -> Correct. `generate_surrogate_key()` creates a deterministic hash (typically MD5) from the concatenation of the provided column values. For the same inputs it always produces the same hash, making it ideal for stable surrogate keys.
  [ ] C. A random UUID generated fresh on every run, unique across all executions
       -> Incorrect. The hash is deterministic, not random -- the same inputs always produce the same output.
  [ ] D. A composite primary key constraint applied to the listed columns in the warehouse
       -> Incorrect. It does not create a database constraint; it generates a computed column value.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `generate_surrogate_key()` does not produce auto-incrementing integers -- it produces hash values. - **B) Correct.** `generate_surrogate_key()` creates a deterministic hash (typically MD5) from the concatenation of the provided column values. For the same inputs it always produces the same hash, making it ideal for stable surrogate keys. - **C) Incorrect.** The hash is deterministic, not random -- the same inputs always produce the same output. - **D) Incorrect.** It does not create a database constraint; it generates a computed column value. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/blog/surrogate-keys

A model `dim_hosts_cleansed` has a contract enforced with these column definitions: - name : host_id data_type : integer - name : host_name data_type : string - name : is_superhost data_type : string - name : updated_at data_type : timestamp - name : created_at data_type : timestamp The model's SELECT includes `NVL(host_name, 'Anonymous') AS host_name`. If a developer adds `LENGTH(host_name) AS name_length` without updating the YAML, what happens?

  [ ] A. The model builds successfully but the `name_length` column is silently dropped from the output
       -> Incorrect. Contracts do not silently drop extra columns. They enforce strict matching between output and the contract definition.
  [ ] B. dbt raises a compilation error before any SQL is executed
       -> Incorrect. The error occurs at execution time, not during compilation. dbt compares actual output columns against the contract after the SQL runs.
  [ ] C. The model builds but dbt issues a warning about the uncontracted column
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not issue a warning for contract violations. It raises an error because contracts are strict enforcement mechanisms.
  [+] D. dbt raises an error during execution because the column is not in the contract
       -> Correct. With `contract: {enforced: true}`, dbt validates that output columns match the YAML contract. A column not in the contract (`name_length`) causes an error at execution time.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Contracts do not silently drop extra columns. They enforce strict matching between output and the contract definition. - **B) Incorrect.** The error occurs at execution time, not during compilation. dbt compares actual output columns against the contract after the SQL runs. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt does not issue a warning for contract violations. It raises an error because contracts are strict enforcement mechanisms. - **D) Correct.** With `contract: {enforced: true}`, dbt validates that output columns match the YAML contract. A column not in the contract (`name_length`) causes an error at execution time. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-contracts#how-are-contracts-enforced

Question 135 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_3.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What is the purpose of `groups` in dbt?

  [+] A. To assign models to a logical grouping that restricts cross-group references based on the `access` config
       -> Correct. Groups organize models into logical collections (e.g., by team ownership). Combined with the `access` config, they control which models can reference each other -- a `private` model can only be referenced within its own group.
  [ ] B. To organize dbt Cloud users into teams for role-based permissions management
       -> Incorrect. Groups are a dbt project-level concept for model governance, not a dbt Cloud user management feature.
  [ ] C. To create parallel execution groups that override thread-based scheduling for faster builds
       -> Incorrect. Groups do not control parallel execution -- dbt handles parallelism via threads and the DAG.
  [ ] D. To tag models for inclusion in specific CI/CD pipelines and deployment environments
       -> Incorrect. Groups are not related to CI/CD pipeline tagging -- use `tags` for that purpose.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Groups organize models into logical collections (e.g., by team ownership). Combined with the `access` config, they control which models can reference each other -- a `private` model can only be referenced within its own group. - **B) Incorrect.** Groups are a dbt project-level concept for model governance, not a dbt Cloud user management feature. - **C) Incorrect.** Groups do not control parallel execution -- dbt handles parallelism via threads and the DAG. - **D) Incorrect.** Groups are not related to CI/CD pipeline tagging -- use `tags` for that purpose. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-access#groups

Question 136 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_3.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
Which TWO constraint types in a dbt model contract are typically enforced by major cloud warehouses (Snowflake, BigQuery, Redshift) at INSERT time? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. `not_null`
       -> Correct. `not_null` is the most consistently enforced constraint across major cloud warehouses at INSERT time.
  [+] B. `check`
       -> Correct. `check` constraints are enforced at INSERT time on platforms that support them (BigQuery, Databricks). They validate that inserted values satisfy a given expression.
  [ ] C. `primary_key`
       -> Incorrect. `primary_key` enforcement varies significantly by platform. On Snowflake and Redshift, it is informational only and not enforced at INSERT time.
  [ ] D. `unique`
       -> Incorrect. `unique` is informational only on Snowflake and Redshift -- they accept duplicate values even when the constraint is declared. Enforcement is not consistent across major warehouses.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `not_null` is the most consistently enforced constraint across major cloud warehouses at INSERT time. - **B) Correct.** `check` constraints are enforced at INSERT time on platforms that support them (BigQuery, Databricks). They validate that inserted values satisfy a given expression. - **C) Incorrect.** `primary_key` enforcement varies significantly by platform. On Snowflake and Redshift, it is informational only and not enforced at INSERT time. - **D) Incorrect.** `unique` is informational only on Snowflake and Redshift -- they accept duplicate values even when the constraint is declared. Enforcement is not consistent across major warehouses. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-contracts#platform-constraint-support

  [ ] D. dbt raises a runtime error when executing `report_monthly` in the warehouse
       -> Incorrect. The error occurs at compilation time, not at runtime. dbt checks access modifiers during graph resolution.

OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** When a model has `access: private`, only models within the same group can reference it. Since `report_monthly` is in a different group, dbt raises a compilation error. - **B) Incorrect.** dbt does not merely warn about private access violations. It raises a hard compilation error preventing the build. - **C) Incorrect.** Being in the same project is not sufficient. `access: private` restricts to the same group, not the same project. - **D) Incorrect.** The error occurs at compilation time, not at runtime. dbt checks access modifiers during graph resolution. Question 138 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_3.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What is the difference between `access: protected` and `access: private` for a model?

  [+] A. `protected` allows access from the same project only; `private` allows access from the same group only
       -> Correct. `access: protected` (the default) allows any model within the same dbt project to reference the model. `access: private` is more restrictive, allowing only models within the same group.
  [ ] B. `protected` allows access from any project; `private` allows access from the same project only
       -> Incorrect. `protected` restricts to the same project, not any project. `access: public` allows cross-project access.
  [ ] C. `protected` and `private` are identical -- both restrict to the same group
       -> Incorrect. `protected` and `private` are different. `protected` allows same-project access; `private` restricts to same-group only.
  [ ] D. `protected` restricts to models in the same directory; `private` restricts to the same YAML file
       -> Incorrect. Access modifiers are based on project and group boundaries, not directory or YAML file locations.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `access: protected` (the default) allows any model within the same dbt project to reference the model. `access: private` is more restrictive, allowing only models within the same group. - **B) Incorrect.** `protected` restricts to the same project, not any project. `access: public` allows cross-project access. - **C) Incorrect.** `protected` and `private` are different. `protected` allows same-project access; `private` restricts to same-group only. - **D) Incorrect.** Access modifiers are based on project and group boundaries, not directory or YAML file locations. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-access

  [ ] D. The model is a Python model that has not been compiled yet
       -> Incorrect. There is no separate compilation step for Python models that would cause this error. Python models compile and execute in one step.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** If the model has never been run, the table/view does not exist in the warehouse, causing a relation-not-found error. - **B) Incorrect.** Ephemeral models are injected as CTEs and would produce a different error pattern, not a relation-not-found error. - **C) Correct.** If the model uses a custom schema, the reference may resolve to the wrong schema location (e.g., `dev_zoltan_staging` instead of `dev_zoltan`). - **D) Incorrect.** There is no separate compilation step for Python models that would cause this error. Python models compile and execute in one step. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/materializations#ephemeral

Question 144 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_4.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
You run a model and see this error: Compilation Error in model mart_fullmoon_reviews ( models / mart / mart_fullmoon_reviews . sql ) Could not render : unexpected char '%' at 18 The model contains this line: COUNT(*) % 7 AS day_of_week_bucket What is causing the error?

  [+] A. The `%` operator is being interpreted as a Jinja delimiter by the template engine
       -> Correct. In Jinja, `%` is part of the block delimiter `{% %}`. The Jinja parser interprets the bare `%` as a block tag, causing a Compilation Error. Use `{{ "%" }}` or `MOD()` instead.
  [ ] B. The `COUNT(*)` function cannot be used with the modulo operator in Snowflake
       -> Incorrect. The `COUNT(*)` function can be used with the modulo operator in Snowflake; the issue is with Jinja parsing, not SQL syntax.
  [ ] C. The `CASE` statement preceding this line has incorrect SQL syntax
       -> Incorrect. The error message references the `%` character specifically, not a preceding CASE statement.
  [ ] D. The model is missing a required `GROUP BY` clause
       -> Incorrect. A missing GROUP BY would produce a Database Error at execution time, not a Compilation Error about an unexpected character.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** In Jinja, `%` is part of the block delimiter `{% %}`. The Jinja parser interprets the bare `%` as a block tag, causing a Compilation Error. Use `{{ "%" }}` or `MOD()` instead. - **B) Incorrect.** The `COUNT(*)` function can be used with the modulo operator in Snowflake; the issue is with Jinja parsing, not SQL syntax. - **C) Incorrect.** The error message references the `%` character specifically, not a preceding CASE statement. - **D) Incorrect.** A missing GROUP BY would produce a Database Error at execution time, not a Compilation Error about an unexpected character. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/jinja-macros#jinja

Question 148 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_4.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A model is configured with `access: private` and assigned to `group: core_data`. A colleague's model in the `reporting` group tries to reference it. What happens?

  [ ] A. The reference works but dbt logs a deprecation warning
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not log a deprecation warning for private model access violations; it fails immediately.
  [ ] B. dbt silently resolves the reference using the public interface
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not silently resolve private model references through a public interface; private models are strictly restricted.
  [ ] C. The reference works in development but fails in production
       -> Incorrect. The restriction is enforced consistently in all environments, not just production. It fails during parsing regardless of the target.
  [+] D. The reference fails with a Compilation Error during parsing
       -> Correct. A model with `access: private` can only be referenced within the same group. A cross-group `ref()` causes a Compilation Error during parsing.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** dbt does not log a deprecation warning for private model access violations; it fails immediately. - **B) Incorrect.** dbt does not silently resolve private model references through a public interface; private models are strictly restricted. - **C) Incorrect.** The restriction is enforced consistently in all environments, not just production. It fails during parsing regardless of the target. - **D) Correct.** A model with `access: private` can only be referenced within the same group. A cross-group `ref()` causes a Compilation Error during parsing. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-access

  [+] A. It takes the UNION of modified models (plus downstream) and previously errored models (plus downstream) -- both sets are included
       -> Correct. A space between `--select` arguments means UNION (OR). Both `state:modified+` and `result:error+` are evaluated, and nodes matching either criterion are selected.
  [ ] B. It further filters to only include modified models that previously errored, plus their downstream dependents
       -> Incorrect. A space means UNION (OR), not further filtering. To get an intersection (AND), you would use a comma separator.
  [ ] C. It takes the INTERSECTION: only models that are both modified AND previously errored, plus their downstream
       -> Incorrect. A space means UNION (OR), not INTERSECTION (AND). The comma operator would create an intersection.
  [ ] D. It overrides `state:modified+` and only runs previously errored models
       -> Incorrect. The second selector does not override the first. Both selectors are combined using UNION logic.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** A space between `--select` arguments means UNION (OR). Both `state:modified+` and `result:error+` are evaluated, and nodes matching either criterion are selected. - **B) Incorrect.** A space means UNION (OR), not further filtering. To get an intersection (AND), you would use a comma separator. - **C) Incorrect.** A space means UNION (OR), not INTERSECTION (AND). The comma operator would create an intersection. - **D) Incorrect.** The second selector does not override the first. Both selectors are combined using UNION logic.        -> Incorrect. REPLACE removes the `$` character, it does not replace numbers with a dollar sign. The cast is to NUMBER, not integer.

       -> Incorrect. REPLACE only removes the specified character (`$`), it does not remove numeric characters.
  [ ] D. It casts the price column to a string data type first, then removes the `$` sign using the REPLACE function
       -> Incorrect. The operations happen in left-to-right order: REPLACE first (removes `$`), then the cast to NUMBER. It does not cast to string first.

Explanation:

Then `:: NUMBER(10, 2)` casts the string to a numeric type with up to 10 total digits and 2 decimal places. - **B) Incorrect.** REPLACE removes the `$` character, it does not replace numbers with a dollar sign. The cast is to NUMBER, not integer. - **C) Incorrect.** REPLACE only removes the specified character (`$`), it does not remove numeric characters. - **D) Incorrect.** The operations happen in left-to-right order: REPLACE first (removes `$`), then the cast to NUMBER. A combined dimension model is materialized as a `view` and performs a LEFT JOIN between listings and hosts. Analysts report slow dashboard queries because the view causes repeated joins at query time. The underlying data changes daily. What is the best materialization change?

  [+] A. Change to `materialized='table'` since the data changes daily and the join cost should be pre-computed once
       -> Correct. Materializing as a `table` pre-computes the join result so analysts query pre-joined data. Since the data changes daily, a nightly table rebuild is appropriate.
  [ ] B. Change to `materialized='incremental'` to only process new rows and avoid rebuilding the full join each run
       -> Incorrect. Incremental adds complexity for a dimension model where both sides of the join can change, making it hard to track what needs reprocessing.

       -> Incorrect. Adding database indexes to a view does not help because views re-execute the underlying query each time they are queried.

Explanation:

  [ ] C. It calculates the time difference between the two timestamps and returns the result as an interval value
       -> Incorrect. `GREATEST` returns a single value (the larger of the two), not a time difference. Date difference would require `DATEDIFF` or subtraction.
  [ ] D. It filters out rows where the host was updated after the listing, keeping only rows where the listing was updated more recently
       -> Incorrect. `GREATEST` is a scalar function in the SELECT clause that returns a value. It does not filter rows.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `GREATEST` returns the largest (most recent) value, not the earliest. `LEAST` would return the earliest date. - **B) Correct.** `GREATEST(l.updated_at, h.updated_at)` returns whichever timestamp is more recent. Date difference would require `DATEDIFF` or subtraction. - **D) Incorrect.** `GREATEST` is a scalar function in the SELECT clause that returns a value. It does not filter rows. Question 163 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
You need a staging model that is only used as an input to a fact model and should never be queried directly. However, you want it to appear in the dbt lineage graph for documentation purposes. Which materialization should you use?

  [ ] A. `ephemeral` -- it will not create a warehouse object but will still appear as a standalone node in the DAG
       -> Incorrect. This statement is contradictory -- ephemeral models are not materialized as queryable objects and are not visible as standalone nodes in the DAG, which is the opposite of the requirement.
  [+] B. `view` -- lightweight and will appear in the DAG; you can restrict access with database grants
       -> Correct. A `view` is lightweight, creates a warehouse object, and appears in the DAG. You can restrict direct access with database grants to discourage direct querying.
  [ ] C. `ephemeral` -- it is not materialized as a queryable object in the warehouse and is not visible as a standalone node in the DAG
       -> Incorrect. While this correctly describes ephemeral behavior, it does not solve the requirement of appearing in the lineage graph as a standalone node.
  [ ] D. `table` -- to ensure it is always available for querying
       -> Incorrect. A table would work but is heavier than necessary for a staging model that should not be queried directly.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** This statement is contradictory -- ephemeral models are not materialized as queryable objects and are not visible as standalone nodes in the DAG, which is the opposite of the requirement. - **B) Correct.** A `view` is lightweight, creates a warehouse object, and appears in the DAG. You can restrict direct access with database grants to discourage direct querying. - **C) Incorrect.** While this correctly describes ephemeral behavior, it does not solve the requirement of appearing in the lineage graph as a standalone node. - **D) Incorrect.** A table would work but is heavier than necessary for a staging model that should not be queried directly. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/materializations#ephemeral

Question 165 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
You need a macro that generates `DATE_TRUNC('month', review_date)` for Snowflake but `DATE_TRUNC(review_date, MONTH)` for BigQuery. What is the recommended dbt pattern?

       -> Incorrect. While `target.type` conditionals work, they become unwieldy as you support more adapters and are not the recommended pattern.
  [+] B. Use the `adapter.dispatch()` pattern with adapter-specific macro implementations
       -> Correct. The recommended pattern is `adapter.dispatch()`, which dispatches to adapter-specific implementations (e.g., `my_macro__snowflake`, `my_macro__bigquery`). This is cleaner and more extensible.
  [ ] C. Write two separate macros: `date_trunc_snowflake` and `date_trunc_bigquery`
       -> Incorrect. Writing separate macros for each adapter requires callers to know which adapter they are on, defeating the purpose of abstraction.

       -> Incorrect. `adapter.quote()` handles identifier quoting, not SQL syntax differences between date functions.

This is cleaner and more extensible. - **C) Incorrect.** Writing separate macros for each adapter requires callers to know which adapter they are on, defeating the purpose of abstraction. - **D) Incorrect.** `adapter.quote()` handles identifier quoting, not SQL syntax differences between date functions. Question 167 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
An incremental reviews model needs to handle late-arriving reviews (up to 48 hours late) and deduplicate reviews with the same surrogate key. Which TWO configurations are most important? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. Add `unique_key='review_id'` (the surrogate key) to enable merge/upsert deduplication on each incremental run
       -> Correct. Setting `unique_key='review_id'` enables merge/upsert deduplication, ensuring that if a late-arriving review matches an existing surrogate key, it updates rather than duplicates.
  [ ] B. Use `incremental_strategy='append'` for maximum insert performance, adding all new rows without deduplication
       -> Incorrect. `append` strategy does not deduplicate -- it only inserts new rows. This would create duplicates when reprocessing late-arriving data.
  [+] C. Add a lookback window in the `is_incremental()` block of at least 48 hours to capture late-arriving data
       -> Correct. A lookback window of at least 48 hours in the `is_incremental()` filter ensures late-arriving rows are captured even when their dates are older than the current maximum.
  [ ] D. Set `materialized='table'` and do a full refresh daily instead of using incremental processing for the model
       -> Incorrect. A full table refresh daily would work but defeats the purpose of incremental processing and is inefficient for large tables.
  [ ] E. Use `on_schema_change='fail'` to prevent any schema changes from being applied during incremental runs
       -> Incorrect. `on_schema_change='fail'` controls behavior when column schemas change, not how late-arriving data is handled.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Setting `unique_key='review_id'` enables merge/upsert deduplication, ensuring that if a late-arriving review matches an existing surrogate key, it updates rather than duplicates. - **B) Incorrect.** `append` strategy does not deduplicate -- it only inserts new rows. This would create duplicates when reprocessing late-arriving data. - **C) Correct.** A lookback window of at least 48 hours in the `is_incremental()` filter ensures late-arriving rows are captured even when their dates are older than the current maximum. - **D) Incorrect.** A full table refresh daily would work but defeats the purpose of incremental processing and is inefficient for large tables. - **E) Incorrect.** `on_schema_change='fail'` controls behavior when column schemas change, not how late-arriving data is handled. What happens when `dbt run` is executed?

  [+] B. dbt raises a contract violation error because the actual `price` data type does not match the declared `numeric` type
       -> Correct. With `contract: {enforced: true}`, dbt validates both column presence and data types against the contract. Returning `price` as `VARCHAR` instead of `numeric` is a type mismatch that causes a contract violation and build failure.
  [ ] C. dbt silently coerces the `price` column from `VARCHAR` to `numeric` at build time using an implicit cast
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not perform silent type coercion. Type mismatches are treated as violations and the build fails immediately.
  [ ] D. The build succeeds but dbt logs a deprecation warning about the type mismatch between `VARCHAR` and `numeric`
       -> Incorrect. Enforced contracts raise hard errors, not warnings. The build exits with a failure status.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** dbt never automatically updates a contract. All contract changes must be made manually in the YAML definition. - **B) Correct.** With `contract: {enforced: true}`, dbt validates both column presence and data types against the contract. Returning `price` as `VARCHAR` instead of `numeric` is a type mismatch that causes a contract violation and build failure. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt does not perform silent type coercion. Type mismatches are treated as violations and the build fails immediately. - **D) Incorrect.** Enforced contracts raise hard errors, not warnings. The build exits with a failure status. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/collaborate/govern/model-contracts

  [ ] D. Contracts only affect documentation generation and have no runtime impact on model builds or data validation
       -> Incorrect. Contracts have real runtime impact through DDL enforcement. They are not documentation-only.

Explanation:

The enforcement happens through DDL, not data validation queries. - **B) Correct.** Model contracts work by modifying the DDL statement used to create the model. dbt generates a `CREATE TABLE ... AS` statement that specifies column types, letting the database enforce type compatibility. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt does not wrap columns in `CAST()` calls. The enforcement is at the DDL level, not by modifying the SELECT statement. - **D) Incorrect.** Contracts have real runtime impact through DDL enforcement. They are not documentation-only.
