Question 176 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
After running `dbt run`, you see: Compilation Error in model src_listings ( models / src / src_listings . sql ) 'listings' is undefined . This can happen when you try to reference a source or model that does not exist , or when you use an undefined variable . The model SQL contains: WITH raw_listings AS ( SELECT * FROM {{ source ( 'airbnb' , listings ) }} ) SELECT id AS listing_id , name AS listing_name FROM raw_listings What is the root cause?

  [+] A. The table name `listings` is missing quotes -- it should be `{{ source('airbnb', 'listings') }}` with both arguments quoted
       -> Correct. Without quotes, Jinja treats `listings` as a variable name and tries to resolve it, resulting in an "undefined" error. The correct syntax is `{{ source('airbnb', 'listings') }}` with both arguments as quoted strings.
  [ ] B. The source `airbnb.listings` is not defined in any `sources.yml` file, so the reference cannot be resolved
       -> Incorrect. The error message says `'listings' is undefined`, which is a Jinja variable resolution error, not a missing source definition error.
  [ ] C. The `source()` function does not accept two arguments -- only the table name should be passed
       -> Incorrect. The `source()` function requires exactly two arguments (source name and table name), and this call does have two arguments -- the issue is the missing quotes.
  [ ] D. The model needs a `config()` block before the SELECT statement to specify the materialization type
       -> Incorrect. A `config()` block is optional. The compilation error is specifically about the unquoted string argument, not a missing config block.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Without quotes, Jinja treats `listings` as a variable name and tries to resolve it, resulting in an "undefined" error. The correct syntax is `{{ source('airbnb', 'listings') }}` with both arguments as quoted strings. - **B) Incorrect.** The error message says `'listings' is undefined`, which is a Jinja variable resolution error, not a missing source definition error. - **C) Incorrect.** The `source()` function requires exactly two arguments (source name and table name), and this call does have two arguments -- the issue is the missing quotes. - **D) Incorrect.** A `config()` block is optional. The compilation error is specifically about the unquoted string argument, not a missing config block. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/dbt-jinja-functions/source

Question 177 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A production run fails with: Database Error in model dim_listings_cleansed ( models / dim / dim_listings_cleansed . sql ) 001003 ( 42000 ): SQL compilation error : syntax error line 15 at position 4 unexpected 'FROM' . The source file looks correct. The error points to line 15 in the compiled SQL. What should you investigate first?

  [ ] A. The `ref()` calls might be resolving to models that do not exist in the warehouse, causing a missing object error
       -> Incorrect. While `ref()` resolution issues can cause errors, the error message specifically mentions a SQL syntax error at a line number, not a missing object.
  [ ] B. Ephemeral upstream models cannot be referenced by table-materialized models due to materialization restrictions
       -> Incorrect. Ephemeral upstream models can be referenced by table models. They are injected as CTEs into the compiled SQL.
  [ ] C. The database does not support CTEs with the `WITH` syntax, causing a compilation error on the compiled SQL
       -> Incorrect. All modern data warehouses support CTEs with the `WITH` syntax. This is not a database compatibility issue.
  [+] D. Check the compiled SQL in `target/compiled/` -- ephemeral CTE injection shifts line numbers from the source file
       -> Correct. Line numbers in database errors refer to the compiled SQL, not the source `.sql` file. Ephemeral CTE injection shifts line numbers. Always check `target/compiled/` to find the actual syntax error.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** While `ref()` resolution issues can cause errors, the error message specifically mentions a SQL syntax error at a line number, not a missing object. - **B) Incorrect.** Ephemeral upstream models can be referenced by table models. They are injected as CTEs into the compiled SQL. - **C) Incorrect.** All modern data warehouses support CTEs with the `WITH` syntax.        -> Incorrect. `dbt run --select result:fail+` requires a `--state` flag pointing to previous run results and is less convenient than `dbt retry` for this use case.

       -> Incorrect. `--fail-fast` causes dbt to stop at the first failure during a run. It does not help recover from a previous failure.

       -> Incorrect. `--full-refresh` rebuilds all incremental models from scratch. It does not target only failed models and is unnecessarily expensive.

  [ ] B. It is built but flagged with a warning status in the run results, allowing downstream models to proceed
       -> Incorrect. `dbt build` does not produce warnings for error-severity test failures -- it treats them as blocking errors.
  [+] C. It is skipped because `dbt build` treats test failures with `error` severity as blocking for downstream nodes
       -> Correct. `dbt build` executes models and tests in DAG order. Test failures with severity `error` are blocking -- downstream models are skipped.
  [ ] D. `dbt build` stops entirely after the first test failure and does not attempt any remaining models in the DAG
       -> Incorrect. `dbt build` does not stop entirely. It skips downstream dependents of the failed test's model but continues building other independent branches of the DAG.

OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** In `dbt build`, tests DO block downstream models when they fail with `error` severity. It skips downstream dependents of the failed test's model but continues building other independent branches of the DAG. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/commands/build

Question 191 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A custom generic test is defined as: {% test positive_values ( model , column_name ) %} SELECT * FROM {{ model }} WHERE {{ column_name }} <= 0 {% endtest %} And used in `schema.yml`: - name : minimum_nights description : '{{ doc("dim_listing_cleansed__minimum_nights") }}' data_tests : - positive_values How does dbt know to pass `minimum_nights` as the `column_name` argument?

  [+] A. When a generic test is listed under a column entry in YAML, dbt automatically passes the column name as `column_name` and the model as `model`
       -> Correct. When a generic test is listed under a specific column in the YAML, dbt automatically provides `model` (the relation) and `column_name` (the column the test is defined under). This convention eliminates the need to explicitly specify these arguments.
  [ ] B. You must explicitly pass `column_name: minimum_nights` in the YAML test configuration for the argument to be provided
       -> Incorrect. Explicit parameter passing is not required for `model` and `column_name` when the test is defined under a column entry. dbt injects them automatically.
  [ ] C. The test reads the column name from the `description` field defined on the same column entry in the schema file
       -> Incorrect. The test does not read from the `description` field. The column name comes from the `name` property of the column entry the test is listed under.
  [ ] D. The `{% test %}` block definition must include a default value for `column_name` or dbt raises a compilation error
       -> Incorrect. The `{% test %}` block does not need a default value for `column_name`. dbt provides the value based on where the test is defined in the YAML hierarchy.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** When a generic test is listed under a specific column in the YAML, dbt automatically provides `model` (the relation) and `column_name` (the column the test is defined under). This convention eliminates the need to explicitly specify these arguments. - **B) Incorrect.** Explicit parameter passing is not required for `model` and `column_name` when the test is defined under a column entry. dbt injects them automatically. - **C) Incorrect.** The test does not read from the `description` field. The column name comes from the `name` property of the column entry the test is listed under. - **D) Incorrect.** The `{% test %}` block does not need a default value for `column_name`. dbt provides the value based on where the test is defined in the YAML hierarchy. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/data-tests#generic-data-tests

Type: SINGLE
A custom generic test is defined with a default severity: {% test minimum_row_count ( model , min_row_count ) %} {{ config ( severity = 'warn' ) }} SELECT COUNT (*) as cnt FROM {{ model }} HAVING COUNT (*) < {{ min_row_count }} {% endtest %} It is used with a YAML-level severity override: data_tests : - minimum_row_count : min_row_count : 1000 config : severity : error What severity will this test use when it runs?

  [ ] A. `warn`, because the macro-level `config(severity = 'warn')` takes precedence over YAML settings
       -> Incorrect. The macro-level `config(severity = 'warn')` sets a default, but it can be overridden by more specific configurations.
  [ ] B. The severity is undefined because there is a conflict between the macro and YAML configs
       -> Incorrect. There is no conflict -- dbt has a clear precedence order where more specific configs override less specific ones.
  [ ] C. It will produce both a warning and an error for the same test execution result
       -> Incorrect. A test produces exactly one result status. It cannot produce both a warning and an error simultaneously.
  [+] D. `error`, because the YAML-level `config: severity: error` overrides the macro-level default setting
       -> Correct. dbt's configuration precedence means more specific configs override less specific ones. The YAML-level `severity: error` overrides the macro's default `severity: warn` for this specific invocation.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The macro-level `config(severity = 'warn')` sets a default, but it can be overridden by more specific configurations. - **B) Incorrect.** There is no conflict -- dbt has a clear precedence order where more specific configs override less specific ones. - **C) Incorrect.** A test produces exactly one result status. It cannot produce both a warning and an error simultaneously. - **D) Correct.** dbt's configuration precedence means more specific configs override less specific ones. The YAML-level `severity: error` overrides the macro's default `severity: warn` for this specific invocation. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-configs/severity

You want to run ONLY the unit tests in your dbt project, without running any data tests (such as `not_null` or `unique`). Which command achieves this?

  [+] A. `dbt test --select test_type:unit`
       -> Correct. `dbt test --select test_type:unit` uses the `test_type` selector to filter to unit tests only. To run only data tests, use `test_type:singular` or `test_type:generic`.
  [ ] B. `dbt unit-test` (dedicated command)
       -> Incorrect. `dbt unit-test` is not a valid dbt CLI command. Unit tests are invoked through `dbt test` with an appropriate selector.
  [ ] C. `dbt test --type unit` (type flag)
       -> Incorrect. `--type` is not a valid flag for `dbt test`. The correct approach is the `--select test_type:unit` selector.
  [ ] D. `dbt run --unit-tests` (run flag)
       -> Incorrect. `dbt run` builds models, not tests. There is no `--unit-tests` flag for `dbt run`.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `dbt test --select test_type:unit` uses the `test_type` selector to filter to unit tests only. To run only data tests, use `test_type:singular` or `test_type:generic`. - **B) Incorrect.** `dbt unit-test` is not a valid dbt CLI command. Unit tests are invoked through `dbt test` with an appropriate selector. - **C) Incorrect.** `--type` is not a valid flag for `dbt test`. The correct approach is the `--select test_type:unit` selector. - **D) Incorrect.** `dbt run` builds models, not tests. There is no `--unit-tests` flag for `dbt run`. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/unit-tests#run-unit-tests

Type: SINGLE
Given this singular test in `tests/consistent_created_at.sql`: SELECT * FROM {{ ref ( 'dim_listings_cleansed' ) }} l INNER JOIN {{ ref ( 'fct_reviews' ) }} r USING ( listing_id ) WHERE l . created_at > r . review_date What business rule does this test validate?

  [ ] A. That every listing in the dimension table has at least one matching review in the fact table (completeness check)
       -> Incorrect. The test does not check if every listing has a review. It checks the temporal relationship between existing listing-review pairs.
  [ ] B. That all review rows in the fact table reference a valid `listing_id` present in the listings dimension table
       -> Incorrect. The JOIN uses `listing_id`, but the test is not about referential integrity. It checks whether review dates precede listing creation dates.
  [+] C. That no review has a `review_date` earlier than the listing's `created_at` -- reviews cannot predate listing creation
       -> Correct. The test returns rows where a listing's `created_at` is later than a review's `review_date`, indicating a review existed before the listing was created. Any returned rows signal a data integrity problem.
  [ ] D. That the `created_at` column contains no null values across the inner join result set between listings and reviews
       -> Incorrect. The test does not check for NULL values. The WHERE clause compares two date columns, not checking for NULLs.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The test does not check if every listing has a review. It checks the temporal relationship between existing listing-review pairs. - **B) Incorrect.** The JOIN uses `listing_id`, but the test is not about referential integrity. It checks whether review dates precede listing creation dates. - **C) Correct.** The test returns rows where a listing's `created_at` is later than a review's `review_date`, indicating a review existed before the listing was created. Any returned rows signal a data integrity problem. - **D) Incorrect.** The test does not check for NULL values. The WHERE clause compares two date columns, not checking for NULLs. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/data-tests#singular-data-tests

Question 195 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A project has this singular test: SELECT * FROM {{ ref ( 'dim_listings_cleansed' ) }} WHERE minimum_nights < 1 LIMIT 10 It also has a `positive_values` generic test on `minimum_nights` that checks `<= 0`. Are these two tests redundant?

  [ ] A. Yes, they test exactly the same condition on the same column and one should be removed to avoid running duplicate checks
       -> Incorrect. The tests are not exactly the same -- they use different comparison operators (`<= 0` vs `< 1`). However, for integer values they produce equivalent results.
  [ ] B. No -- the generic test checks `<= 0` while the singular test checks `< 1`, making the singular test stricter for all data types
       -> Incorrect. This correctly identifies the different operators but incorrectly claims the singular test is strictly more restrictive without considering the data type.
  [+] C. No -- the generic test checks `<= 0` and the singular test checks `< 1`, but since `minimum_nights` is an integer, both are equivalent
       -> Correct. For integer values, `<= 0` and `< 1` produce the same results. The `LIMIT 10` only affects how many failing rows are returned, not whether the test passes or fails.
  [ ] D. The singular test is more restrictive because the `LIMIT 10` clause means it only flags the test when at least 10 violations exist
       -> Incorrect. `LIMIT 10` does not make the test more restrictive. A test passes when zero rows are returned and fails when any rows are returned, regardless of LIMIT.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The tests are not exactly the same -- they use different comparison operators (`<= 0` vs `< 1`). However, for integer values they produce equivalent results. - **B) Incorrect.** This correctly identifies the different operators but incorrectly claims the singular test is strictly more restrictive without considering the data type. - **C) Correct.** For integer values, `<= 0` and `< 1` produce the same results. The `LIMIT 10` only affects how many failing rows are returned, not whether the test passes or fails. - **D) Incorrect.** `LIMIT 10` does not make the test more restrictive. A test passes when zero rows are returned and fails when any rows are returned, regardless of LIMIT. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/data-tests

Question 196 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
When are singular tests the better choice over generic tests? (Choose 2)

  [ ] A. Validating that `listing_id` is unique in a dimension model, with no duplicate values allowed
       -> Incorrect. Validating uniqueness is a standard pattern perfectly suited for the built-in `unique` generic test.
  [+] B. Validating a complex cross-model business rule that checks listing creation dates against review dates
       -> Correct. Cross-model business rules involving JOINs between models and complex WHERE conditions are ideal for singular tests, as they cannot be expressed with generic test parameters.
  [ ] C. Validating that `room_type` is one of four known values across all listing models in the project
       -> Incorrect. Validating accepted values across multiple models is a standard pattern suited for the `accepted_values` generic test applied to each model.
  [+] D. Validating that no listing has a `minimum_nights` value exceeding 365 -- a rule specific to one model
       -> Correct. A model-specific rule like maximum `minimum_nights` value is a one-off business rule that is simpler to express as a singular test SQL query.
  [ ] E. Validating that `host_id` is not null across all dimension models that contain a host reference
       -> Incorrect. Validating not-null across multiple models is a standard reusable pattern perfectly suited for the `not_null` generic test.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Validating uniqueness is a standard pattern perfectly suited for the built-in `unique` generic test. - **B) Correct.** Cross-model business rules involving JOINs between models and complex WHERE conditions are ideal for singular tests, as they cannot be expressed with generic test parameters. - **C) Incorrect.** Validating accepted values across multiple models is a standard pattern suited for the `accepted_values` generic test applied to each model. - **D) Correct.** A model-specific rule like maximum `minimum_nights` value is a one-off business rule that is simpler to express as a singular test SQL query. - **E) Incorrect.** Validating not-null across multiple models is a standard reusable pattern perfectly suited for the `not_null` generic test. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/data-tests#singular-data-tests

       -> Incorrect. The freshness check is not disabled -- the `warn_after` threshold is still active and will report a warning status.
  [+] D. Warn, because 12 hours exceeds the 1-hour `warn_after` threshold, but no `error_after` threshold is configured to trigger an error

When `error_after` is not configured, no error threshold exists. - **C) Incorrect.** The freshness check is not disabled -- the `warn_after` threshold is still active and will report a warning status. - **D) Correct.** With only `warn_after` active, the check can never produce an `error` -- only `warn` or `pass`. Since 12 hours exceeds the 1-hour threshold, the result is `warn`. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/sources#source-freshness

Question 198 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Given this referential integrity test configuration: - name : fct_reviews columns : - name : listing_id data_tests : - relationships : to : ref ( 'dim_listings_cleansed' ) field : listing_id What does this test validate?

  [ ] A. That the `listing_id` column contains no null values in `fct_reviews` (null check)
       -> Incorrect. Null checking is the job of the `not_null` test. The `relationships` test only validates non-null values against the reference table; null values are excluded from the check.
  [ ] B. That the `listing_id` values are unique across all rows in `fct_reviews`
       -> Incorrect. Uniqueness is validated by the `unique` test. The `relationships` test validates referential integrity across tables.
  [+] C. That every non-null `listing_id` in `fct_reviews` exists in `dim_listings_cleansed`
       -> Correct. The `relationships` test is dbt's built-in referential integrity check. It verifies that every non-null value in `fct_reviews.listing_id` has a matching row in `dim_listings_cleansed.listing_id`. It fails if any review references a listing that does not exist in the dimension table.
  [ ] D. That the total row count of `fct_reviews` matches the row count of `dim_listings_cleansed`
       -> Incorrect. Row count comparison uses `dbt_expectations.expect_table_row_count_to_equal_other_table`. The `relationships` test validates key existence, not row counts.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** Null checking is the job of the `not_null` test. The `relationships` test only validates non-null values against the reference table; null values are excluded from the check. - **B) Incorrect.** Uniqueness is validated by the `unique` test. The `relationships` test validates referential integrity across tables. - **C) Correct.** The `relationships` test is dbt's built-in referential integrity check. It verifies that every non-null value in `fct_reviews.listing_id` has a matching row in `dim_listings_cleansed.listing_id`. It fails if any review references a listing that does not exist in the dimension table. - **D) Incorrect.** Row count comparison uses `dbt_expectations.expect_table_row_count_to_equal_other_table`. The `relationships` test validates key existence, not row counts. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-properties/data-tests#relationships

       -> Correct. Ephemeral models are not materialized as queryable warehouse objects and do not appear as standalone nodes in the lineage graph. They are compiled as CTEs into downstream models.

Ephemeral models are excluded by design. - **D) Correct.** Ephemeral models are not materialized as queryable warehouse objects and do not appear as standalone nodes in the lineage graph. Type: SINGLE
When you run `dbt build --select +exposure:executive_dashboard`, what will happen?

  [+] A. All upstream ancestors of both dependent models AND those two models themselves will be built and tested in DAG order
       -> Correct. The `+` prefix means "include parents." This selects the exposure's dependent models AND all their upstream ancestors. `dbt build` then runs and tests them in DAG order.
  [ ] B. Only the two models listed in the exposure's `depends_on` will be built, without including their upstream ancestors
       -> Incorrect. Without the `+` prefix, only the two dependent models would be selected. The `+` operator adds all upstream ancestors.
  [ ] C. Only the most recently modified model among the exposure's dependencies will be built and tested
       -> Incorrect. The selection includes all upstream ancestors of the exposure's dependencies, not just the most recently modified model.
  [ ] D. The exposure will reject the build because `maturity: low` means the dashboard is not ready for production use
       -> Incorrect. The `maturity` property is informational only and does not affect model selection or build behavior.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** The `+` prefix means "include parents." This selects the exposure's dependent models AND all their upstream ancestors. `dbt build` then runs and tests them in DAG order. - **B) Incorrect.** Without the `+` prefix, only the two dependent models would be selected. The `+` operator adds all upstream ancestors. - **C) Incorrect.** The selection includes all upstream ancestors of the exposure's dependencies, not just the most recently modified model. - **D) Incorrect.** The `maturity` property is informational only and does not affect model selection or build behavior. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/exposures

Question 205 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Given these `dbt_expectations` tests on a `price` column: - name : price data_tests : - dbt_expectations . expect_column_values_to_be_of_type : column_type : number - dbt_expectations . expect_column_quantile_values_to_be_between : quantile : . 99 min_value : 50 max_value : 500 - dbt_expectations . expect_column_max_to_be_between : max_value : 5000 config : severity : warn If the maximum price in the data is $6,000, which tests will fail?

  [ ] A. All three tests will fail
       -> Incorrect. The type check passes because it checks the data type (number), not the actual values. The quantile test likely passes because a single outlier may not push the 99th percentile above $500.
  [ ] B. None will fail -- `expect_column_max_to_be_between` only warns, which is not a failure
       -> Incorrect. `expect_column_max_to_be_between` does produce a result -- it warns because $6,000 exceeds $5,000. A warn IS a non-pass status.
  [ ] C. Only `expect_column_quantile_values_to_be_between` will fail because $6,000 pushes the 99th percentile above $500
       -> Incorrect. A single $6,000 outlier is unlikely to push the 99th percentile above $500 if most prices are below that range. The quantile test likely passes.
  [+] D. Only `expect_column_max_to_be_between` will warn because $6,000 exceeds `max_value: 5000`
       -> Correct. The type check passes (checks data type, not values). The 99th percentile can still be within $50-$500 even with a single outlier. Only `expect_column_max_to_be_between` triggers because $6,000 exceeds $5,000, but its severity is `warn`.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The type check passes because it checks the data type (number), not the actual values. The quantile test likely passes because a single outlier may not push the 99th percentile above $500. - **B) Incorrect.** `expect_column_max_to_be_between` does produce a result -- it warns because $6,000 exceeds $5,000. A warn IS a non-pass status. - **C) Incorrect.** A single $6,000 outlier is unlikely to push the 99th percentile above $500 if most prices are below that range. The quantile test likely passes. - **D) Correct.** The type check passes (checks data type, not values). The 99th percentile can still be within $50-$500 even with a single outlier. Only `expect_column_max_to_be_between` triggers because $6,000 exceeds $5,000, but its severity is `warn`. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-configs/severity

Question 206 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
Given this snapshot configuration: snapshots : - name : scd_raw_listings relation : source ( 'airbnb' , 'listings' ) config : unique_key : id strategy : timestamp updated_at : updated_at hard_deletes : invalidate What type of slowly changing dimension does this implement, and what happens when a source row is deleted?

  [ ] A. SCD Type 1 -- overwrites old values in place; deleted source rows are physically removed from the snapshot table
       -> Incorrect. SCD Type 1 overwrites old values without maintaining history. The `timestamp` strategy with `dbt_valid_from`/`dbt_valid_to` columns is SCD Type 2.
  [ ] B. SCD Type 2 -- maintains row history for changes, but deleted source rows are physically removed from the snapshot table
       -> Incorrect. While this is SCD Type 2, `hard_deletes: invalidate` does NOT physically remove rows. It sets `dbt_valid_to` to mark them as invalidated.
  [ ] C. SCD Type 3 -- stores both the current and previous values as separate columns in the same row of the snapshot table
       -> Incorrect. SCD Type 3 stores current and previous values in the same row using additional columns. The `timestamp` strategy creates new rows for each change, which is SCD Type 2.
  [+] D. SCD Type 2 -- maintains history via new rows for changes; deleted source rows have `dbt_valid_to` set rather than being removed
       -> Correct. The `timestamp` strategy implements SCD Type 2 with row versioning. The `hard_deletes: invalidate` option marks deleted source rows by setting `dbt_valid_to` rather than physically removing them.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** SCD Type 1 overwrites old values without maintaining history. The `timestamp` strategy with `dbt_valid_from`/`dbt_valid_to` columns is SCD Type 2. - **B) Incorrect.** While this is SCD Type 2, `hard_deletes: invalidate` does NOT physically remove rows. It sets `dbt_valid_to` to mark them as invalidated. - **C) Incorrect.** SCD Type 3 stores current and previous values in the same row using additional columns. The `timestamp` strategy creates new rows for each change, which is SCD Type 2. - **D) Correct.** The `timestamp` strategy implements SCD Type 2 with row versioning. The `hard_deletes: invalidate` option marks deleted source rows by setting `dbt_valid_to` rather than physically removing them. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/docs/build/snapshots

Question 207 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A source test uses a regex validation: sources : - name : airbnb tables : - name : listings columns : - name : price data_tests : - dbt_expectations . expect_column_values_to_match_regex : regex : "^\\$[0-9][0-9\\.]+$" What does this regex validate about the `price` column?

  [ ] A. That prices are plain numbers without any currency symbol, matching values like `123.45` or `99`
       -> Incorrect. The regex requires a literal `$` at the start of the string, so plain numbers without a dollar sign would not match.
  [ ] B. That prices are in a currency format including commas as thousands separators, like `$1,234.56`
       -> Incorrect. The regex does not include a comma character class, so prices with commas like `$1,234.56` would not match.
  [ ] C. That prices contain a dollar sign and exactly two decimal places after a required decimal point
       -> Incorrect. The regex does not enforce exactly two decimal places. The `[0-9\.]+` pattern allows any number of digits and dots.
  [+] D. That prices start with a dollar sign followed by at least two digits and optional decimal, like `$12.50`
       -> Correct. The regex (after YAML escaping) matches strings starting with a literal `$`, followed by a digit, then one or more digits or dots, validating patterns like `$12.50` and `$100`.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** The regex requires a literal `$` at the start of the string, so plain numbers without a dollar sign would not match. - **B) Incorrect.** The regex does not include a comma character class, so prices with commas like `$1,234.56` would not match. - **C) Incorrect.** The regex does not enforce exactly two decimal places. The `[0-9\.]+` pattern allows any number of digits and dots. - **D) Correct.** The regex (after YAML escaping) matches strings starting with a literal `$`, followed by a digit, then one or more digits or dots, validating patterns like `$12.50` and `$100`. Reference: https://github.com/calogica/dbt-expectations

  [ ] A. Test results are stored directly in a schema called `test_audit` within the target database, with only failing rows saved as tables
       -> Incorrect. While close, this answer incorrectly describes the schema. The `+schema` config does not place results directly in `test_audit` -- it uses the default `generate_schema_name` behavior.
  [ ] B. All test SQL definitions are written to a `test_audit` folder in the project directory for offline review and debugging
       -> Incorrect. `store_failures` writes to the database, not to files in the project directory.
  [ ] C. Tests are only run against models that exist in the `test_audit` schema, skipping models in other schemas
       -> Incorrect. Tests still run against their configured models. The `+schema` config only controls where failure results are stored, not what schema tests run against.
  [+] D. Failing rows are written to tables in `<target_schema>_test_audit`, overriding the default `dbt_test__audit` schema name
       -> Correct. With `store_failures: true`, dbt stores failing rows as tables. The `+schema: test_audit` overrides the default `dbt_test__audit` schema name. The default `generate_schema_name` concatenates `target.schema` + `_` + the custom schema.

OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** While close, this answer incorrectly describes the schema. The `+schema` config does not place results directly in `test_audit` -- it uses the default `generate_schema_name` behavior. - **B) Incorrect.** `store_failures` writes to the database, not to files in the project directory. - **C) Incorrect.** Tests still run against their configured models. The `+schema` config only controls where failure results are stored, not what schema tests run against. - **D) Correct.** With `store_failures: true`, dbt stores failing rows as tables. The `+schema: test_audit` overrides the default `dbt_test__audit` schema name. The default `generate_schema_name` concatenates `target.schema` + `_` + the custom schema. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/resource-configs/store_failures

Question 209 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A developer wants to test changes to `fct_reviews` locally without building all 15 upstream models from scratch. Their company stores production artifacts in S3, which have been downloaded to `./prod-artifacts/`. Which command allows `fct_reviews` to reference production-built upstream tables instead of rebuilding them locally?

  [+] A. `dbt run --select fct_reviews --defer --state ./prod-artifacts`
       -> Correct. `--defer` combined with `--state` tells dbt to resolve any `ref()` that would point to a model NOT in the current selection to the corresponding object from the production environment (from the state artifacts). This allows building only `fct_reviews` locally while its upstream models are resolved from production.
  [ ] B. `dbt run --select fct_reviews --skip-upstream` (skip flag)
       -> Incorrect. `--skip-upstream` is not a valid dbt flag.
  [ ] C. `dbt run --select fct_reviews --no-deps` (no-deps flag)
       -> Incorrect. `--no-deps` is not a valid dbt flag.
  [ ] D. `dbt run --select +fct_reviews --state ./prod-artifacts`
       -> Incorrect. `--select +fct_reviews` selects all upstream models too, which defeats the purpose of deferring. Without `--defer`, upstream models would need to be built locally.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `--defer` combined with `--state` tells dbt to resolve any `ref()` that would point to a model NOT in the current selection to the corresponding object from the production environment (from the state artifacts). This allows building only `fct_reviews` locally while its upstream models are resolved from production. - **B) Incorrect.** `--skip-upstream` is not a valid dbt flag. - **C) Incorrect.** `--no-deps` is not a valid dbt flag. - **D) Incorrect.** `--select +fct_reviews` selects all upstream models too, which defeats the purpose of deferring. Without `--defer`, upstream models would need to be built locally. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/defer

Question 210 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
You make the following changes in a PR: (1) change the SQL logic in `dim_listings_cleansed.sql`, (2) add a new column description to `dim_hosts_cleansed` in the YAML without changing any SQL, (3) add a new model `dim_neighborhoods`. Which models will `state:modified` select? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. `dim_listings_cleansed` -- because its SQL logic changed
       -> Correct. `dim_listings_cleansed` is selected because its SQL logic changed, which alters its compiled state compared to the reference manifest.
  [ ] B. `dim_hosts_cleansed` -- because its YAML properties changed
       -> Incorrect. Description-only YAML changes do not alter the model's compiled state. `state:modified` compares compiled representations, not documentation metadata.
  [+] C. `dim_neighborhoods` -- because it is a new model not in the reference state
       -> Correct. `dim_neighborhoods` is a new model not present in the reference state, so `state:modified` identifies it as modified (new).
  [ ] D. All downstream models of `dim_listings_cleansed`
       -> Incorrect. `state:modified` does not include downstream models automatically. The `+` operator would be needed to include dependents.
  [ ] E. Only `dim_neighborhoods` because it is the only structurally new model
       -> Incorrect. Both `dim_listings_cleansed` (modified SQL) and `dim_neighborhoods` (new model) are selected, not just the new model.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** `dim_listings_cleansed` is selected because its SQL logic changed, which alters its compiled state compared to the reference manifest. - **B) Incorrect.** Description-only YAML changes do not alter the model's compiled state. `state:modified` compares compiled representations, not documentation metadata. - **C) Correct.** `dim_neighborhoods` is a new model not present in the reference state, so `state:modified` identifies it as modified (new). - **D) Incorrect.** `state:modified` does not include downstream models automatically. The `+` operator would be needed to include dependents. - **E) Incorrect.** Both `dim_listings_cleansed` (modified SQL) and `dim_neighborhoods` (new model) are selected, not just the new model. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/methods#the-state-method

Question 211 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
What does the `--favor-state` flag do beyond what `--defer` already provides?

  [ ] A. It forces dbt to always use production models for every ref, even for models that are included in the current run selection
       -> Incorrect. `--favor-state` does not force ALL models to use production. It only affects unmodified models that are not part of the current selection.
  [ ] B. It skips all tests during CI to speed up the pipeline execution time when building modified models and their dependents
       -> Incorrect. `--favor-state` has nothing to do with skipping tests. It controls how unselected model refs are resolved.
  [+] C. It makes dbt prefer the state artifact's version of unselected models even if a stale copy exists in the current target
       -> Correct. With `--defer` alone, dbt only falls back to the state artifact when the model does not exist in the current target. `--favor-state` goes further and prefers the state artifact even if a stale copy exists.
  [ ] D. It downloads production table data into the CI environment so that models can be built and tested against local data copies
       -> Incorrect. `--favor-state` does not download or copy production data. It controls reference resolution at compile time.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `--favor-state` does not force ALL models to use production. It only affects unmodified models that are not part of the current selection. - **B) Incorrect.** `--favor-state` has nothing to do with skipping tests. It controls how unselected model refs are resolved. - **C) Correct.** With `--defer` alone, dbt only falls back to the state artifact when the model does not exist in the current target. `--favor-state` goes further and prefers the state artifact even if a stale copy exists. - **D) Incorrect.** `--favor-state` does not download or copy production data. It controls reference resolution at compile time. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/defer

Question 212 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A production run resulted in 30 models succeeding, 1 failing (`fct_reviews`), and 15 being skipped. You run: dbt retry How many models will dbt attempt to build?

  [ ] A. All 46 models from the full original run, including the 30 that succeeded
       -> Incorrect. `dbt retry` does not re-run the full original set. It only re-runs nodes that were not successful.
  [ ] B. Only the 1 failed model (`fct_reviews`), skipping all others
       -> Incorrect. `dbt retry` includes both failed models AND models that were skipped due to upstream failures, not just the directly failed model.
  [+] C. The 1 failed model and the 15 skipped models (16 total), excluding the 30 successes
       -> Correct. `dbt retry` re-executes nodes that were not successful: both the 1 failed model AND the 15 skipped models (16 total). The 30 already-successful models are not re-run.
  [ ] D. Only the 15 skipped models, since the failed model already attempted execution
       -> Incorrect. The skipped models depended on the failed model. `dbt retry` re-runs the failed model first, then attempts the skipped downstream models.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `dbt retry` does not re-run the full original set. It only re-runs nodes that were not successful. - **B) Incorrect.** `dbt retry` includes both failed models AND models that were skipped due to upstream failures, not just the directly failed model. - **C) Correct.** `dbt retry` re-executes nodes that were not successful: both the 1 failed model AND the 15 skipped models (16 total). The 30 already-successful models are not re-run. - **D) Incorrect.** The skipped models depended on the failed model. `dbt retry` re-runs the failed model first, then attempts the skipped downstream models. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/commands/retry

During the CI run, `ref('dim_hosts_cleansed')` inside `dim_listings_w_hosts` resolves to the production schema. Why?

  [ ] A. The `--defer` flag is broken and always resolves all `ref()` calls to production regardless of model selection
       -> Incorrect. `--defer` does not resolve ALL refs to production. It only falls back for models not built in the current invocation.
  [ ] B. The CI schema does not have the `dim_hosts_cleansed` table, so dbt falls back to the default target schema instead
       -> Incorrect. While the CI schema does not have the table, the reason is specifically because `--defer` resolves unselected model refs to the production state manifest, not a generic fallback behavior.
  [+] C. Because `dim_hosts_cleansed` was not modified and not selected, `--defer` resolves its ref to the production state manifest
       -> Correct. Because `dim_hosts_cleansed` was not modified and not selected, `--defer` resolves its `ref()` to the production relation from the state manifest.
  [ ] D. `dim_listings_w_hosts` was excluded from the selection because it is not directly modified in the pull request
       -> Incorrect. `dim_listings_w_hosts` IS included because it depends on the modified `dim_listings_cleansed` (via the `+` in `state:modified+`).

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Incorrect.** `--defer` does not resolve ALL refs to production. It only falls back for models not built in the current invocation. - **B) Incorrect.** While the CI schema does not have the table, the reason is specifically because `--defer` resolves unselected model refs to the production state manifest, not a generic fallback behavior. - **C) Correct.** Because `dim_hosts_cleansed` was not modified and not selected, `--defer` resolves its `ref()` to the production relation from the state manifest. - **D) Incorrect.** `dim_listings_w_hosts` IS included because it depends on the modified `dim_listings_cleansed` (via the `+` in `state:modified+`). Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/defer

Question 215 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: MULTIPLE
A CI pipeline uses `--defer` with `--state` pointing to production artifacts. A modified model references an ephemeral staging model, which references `source('airbnb', 'listings')`. Which TWO statements are correct? (Choose 2)

  [+] A. The ephemeral model's SQL is still injected as a CTE even with `--defer`, because ephemeral models are compiled inline rather than resolved as relations
       -> Correct. Ephemeral models are CTEs injected inline, so they compile into the consuming model even when deferred. They are not separate relations that need deferral.
  [+] B. The `source()` call always resolves to the actual source table regardless of `--defer`, because sources are external data, not dbt models
       -> Correct. Source references via `source()` always resolve to the configured source location regardless of `--defer`, because sources are external data tables, not dbt models.
  [ ] C. dbt automatically rebuilds all ephemeral upstream models as separate objects in the CI environment before building the modified model
       -> Incorrect. dbt does not "rebuild" ephemeral models -- they are compiled as CTEs into the consuming model. There is no separate build step for ephemeral models.
  [ ] D. `--defer` converts ephemeral models into table materializations for the CI run so they can be referenced as standalone objects
       -> Incorrect. `--defer` does not change materialization strategies. Ephemeral models remain ephemeral regardless of the `--defer` flag.
  [ ] E. `--defer` is only available in dbt Cloud and cannot be used with dbt Core, so this pipeline requires a Cloud environment
       -> Incorrect. `--defer` is available in both dbt Core and dbt Cloud. It is not a Cloud-only feature.

Explanation:
OVERALL: - **A) Correct.** Ephemeral models are CTEs injected inline, so they compile into the consuming model even when deferred. They are not separate relations that need deferral. - **B) Correct.** Source references via `source()` always resolve to the configured source location regardless of `--defer`, because sources are external data tables, not dbt models. - **C) Incorrect.** dbt does not "rebuild" ephemeral models -- they are compiled as CTEs into the consuming model. There is no separate build step for ephemeral models. - **D) Incorrect.** `--defer` does not change materialization strategies. Ephemeral models remain ephemeral regardless of the `--defer` flag. - **E) Incorrect.** `--defer` is available in both dbt Core and dbt Cloud. It is not a Cloud-only feature. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/defer

Question 216 (from Course_ 2026 dbt Analytics Engineering Certification Practice Tests _ Udemy Business_5.mhtml):
Type: SINGLE
A developer modifies only the SQL in `dim_hosts_cleansed` and runs a Slim CI build: dbt build --select state:modified+ --state ./prod-artifacts/ Looking at the lineage graph above, which models does `state:modified+` select?

  [ ] A. Only `dim_hosts_cleansed` (the modified model alone, no downstream dependents)
       -> Incorrect. Without the `+` suffix, `state:modified` alone would select only the modified model. The `+` adds downstream dependents.
  [+] B. `dim_hosts_cleansed` and the downstream dependents
       -> Correct. `state:modified` identifies `dim_hosts_cleansed` as modified. The `+` suffix adds its downstream dependents.
  [ ] C. `dim_hosts_cleansed` + all dependents + `dim_listings_w_hosts` + all of it dependends, because they share downstream models
       -> Incorrect. `dim_listings_cleansed` is not downstream of `dim_hosts_cleansed` — it is a separate upstream input to `dim_listings_w_hosts` on a different branch.
  [ ] D. dbt doesn't support the + notation along with the ":modified" notation
       -> Incorrect. `state:modified` does support the "+" notation and identifies `dim_hosts_cleansed` as modified. The `+` suffix adds its downstream dependents.

Explanation:
OVERALL: `state:modified` does support the "+" notation and identifies `dim_hosts_cleansed` as modified. The `+` suffix adds its downstream dependents. Reference: https://docs.getdbt.com/reference/node-selection/methods#the-state-method
